"Here is a 6A framework we use to create an account-based playbook:


Pre-requisites:


- Formed ABM team
- Defined program goals (new logo, expansion, acceleration)
- Defined cluster or vertical
- Cluster win/loss deal analysis


6 playbook pillars.


1. ACCOUNT QUALIFICATION.


- Firmo and technographics
- Qualification criteria / signals
- Disqualification criteria
- Tier segmentation
- Buying committee structure


2. ACCOUNT SEGMENTATION.


Segment all accounts by Tiers, Vendor Awareness, Relationship and  Product-Need Evidence signals.


1. Cluster ICP accounts (Not aware of us & product need is unknown).
2. Future Pipeline accounts (Aware of us & product need is unknown).
3. Active Focus accounts (Aware of us and the product need is known).


3. ACCOUNT RESEARCH.


Define information you absolutely must know about an account to create a personalized offer:


- Strategic initiatives and priorities
- Challenges
- Jobs-to-be-done & KPis of target buyer persona
- Other account enrichment information


Split it into desk and 1-1 research.


4. ACCOUNT AWARENESS.


Define core activities and content to create awareness among buying committee members.


5. ACCOUNT DEVELOPMENT.


Define key activities to engage buying committee members and build a relationship with them.


6. ACCOUNT ACTIVATION.


Personalize your offer and define bridge activities to book discovery meetings.
----
Most ABM playbooks I've seen are not well thought and traditionally fail because:


- Lack of committed pilot team (especially ABM lead and SDR role) preventing proper program execution and making ABM efforts a low-priority burden.


- No clear playbooks for accounts that are different journey stages (not vendor aware, not in market)


- Target account list is too broad and mixes different segments, which dilutes focus.


- No proactive sales engagement.


- Lack of account research and personalization leads to sending the same message to all the accounts.


- Missing personalized account development processes for engaged accounts causing potential opportunities to stall in basic email nurture.


ABM is not a fancy wrapping for lead gen.


If you want to land enterprise deals, be ready to roll up your sleeves and do the necessary work.

"Here is a detailed playbook of 4 ABM programs that generated over 7mln pipeline during the pilot:




1. COMMITTED PILOT TEAM.


With every client, we had a pilot ABM team including:


-ABM lead
-Content marketer
-SDR or AE


with operational support from:


-Subject-Matter Expert
-RevOps (In some teams, the RevOps function was executed by the ABM lead).


Pilot team spent at least 60% of its time working on the ABM program.
Commitment is the key.


2. FOCUSING ON ACCOUNTS WITH HIGH PROBABILITY TO BECOME A SALES OPPORTUNITY.


Instead of engaging hundreds of ""it's a perfect ICP match"" accounts, we defined accounts that:


-Have high revenue potential (Tier 1 and Tier 2).
-Know us (hit our engagement threshold).
-We have some level of relationship with the buying committee member.
-There is clear evidence of the challenge or inefficiency that our product can help with.


We ran only 1:1 playbooks with fully personalized content and engagement to drive sales opportunities.


3. MIX OF PLAYBOOKS TO DRIVE BUYING COMMITTEE AWARENESS AND ENGAGEMENT.


The biggest mistake with ABM is treating all accounts the same way and running the same playbooks.


We split other accounts into two groups and ran a mix of playbooks to connect and engage buying committee members, including:


-Cluster (use-case/challenge-based) content
-Cluster webinars or in-person events
-Buyer interviews and collaborations with internal marketing teams to spread awareness
-Constant engagement and content distribution to open conversations


For these two segments, the core KPI was achieving # of accounts that hit our engagement threshold instead of trying to generate a sales opportunity with them.


4. WE TURNED EVERY WEEK INTO A SPRINT.


We met with a pilot team every week to:


-Track our progress and weekly KPIs
-Review and fix bottlenecks
-Cross-share newly collected account insights and engagement
-Plan next week including account engagement, playbooks, content, etc.
-Define and report internally on small wins to generate more interest and support for ABM
---
We've interviewed our clients Divash Basnet, Lee Adam, Amy Leyh Loesch, Ellen Kaross, João Crisóstomo, Ken Roden to share with you behind-the-scenes of the programs and the necessary internal change management.

"We never work with B2B companies that reach out to us and ask ""to generate more leads"". Here is why.


""LEADS"" are the consequence of brand awareness, demand generation, joint marketing and sales nurturing and activation, buyer enablement, customer advocacy, and a great product.


LEADS are a lagging indicator of your marketing & sales efficiency.


Your buyer pre-select you or your competitor way before you become aware of it.


""LEADS"" become interested in your product not because they saw an ad telling how great your product is or received ""personalized"" cold email from SDR.


They become interested when they believe your product is one of the best possible solutions to their challenges.


Lead generation is not a linear function. At least, not in enterprise B2B sales and marketing (though it might be different for $15 SaaS).


Automated outbound cadences amplified by multichannel ads won't grow your pipeline.


To compete and grow in 2025, you must replace the lead gen with multithreaded full-funnel marketing.


Here are 7 principles.


1. Everybody who interacts with customers works on pipeline and revenue generation.


2. ICP (Ideal Customer Profile) and buyer journey dictate your marketing and sales programs, not the opposite. Customer research is not a ""nice to have"" but a critical element of your GTM strategy.


3. Last click attribution is replaced with a holistic revenue report. Not every click or email should produce a meeting. Call to actions are aligned with the buyer journey stage.


4. Quality > Quantity. Content, messaging, events are co-created with subject-matter experts, industry thought leaders and your buyers. It takes more time, but it creates content and messaging that resonates.


5. Account prioritization. Both marketing and sales define critieria of accounts that are likely to become sales opportunities and spend 80% of their time working on them instead of targeting ""wish lists"".


6. Buyer enablement instead of sales enablement. 


7. Expansion and retention are active functions. 
------


Decade ago B2B companies operated in a siloed GTM with ""predictable revenue"" model.


Marketing and sales programs were prioritized by last-click attribution, stimulating credit fights.


Most B2B companies ignored brand awareness and demand generation activities while they were growing.


What has changed in the last 15 years?


Cost of acquisition through siloed programs drastically increased.


Cold outbound produces <1% discovery to closed won opportunities.


As a consequence, companies that fostered marketing and sales silos, were laying off their SDRs and marketers last year.


You either wake up from a lead generation hangover, take the red pill and adjust your marketing and sales to how your customers are buying or wait until the next layoff round.
----
If you want to learn about what actually works in B2B marketing, sign up for our virtual Full-Funnel Summit: https://lnkd.in/ddZ6Qyk8"

"Last ABM program we ran with João Crisóstomo for ICP that is not active on social generated 14 sales-qualified leads, 4 sales opportunities, 1 closed won and app. $1.7 mln pipeline in 90 days. Here is what we did:


Before diving deeper, here is a context.


The company tried ABM before, but it didn't work. Some of the root reasons:


- lack of marketing and sales alignment and joint collaboration
- unsuccesful outbound to a technical audience that hates to engage with sales reps without domain knowledge
- too broad ICP
- buyer personas are not active on social


Here are 5 things we did that most ABM teams never do:


1. We didn't target verticals, but targeted clusters.


Clusters = companies that fit your ICP and have a similar challenge. We interviewed our solution architect (SME) and defined a cluster where we had a competitive advantage. Then, we looked at the verticals where this challenge is more vivid and painful (in our case, regulated industries).


We did together challenge decomposition by reviewing: 


- the broken workflows our target buyers might have
- the root reasons behind them
- jobs-to-be-done and how they might be improved


That helped us to define content topics and messaging that are relevant to these buyers.


2. We didn't target every account that fits ICP, but focused on those who know us and demonstrate product-need evidence.


Instead of targeting a wish list of accounts, we looked at accounts that: 


- hit our engagement threshold
- meet one of the qualification criteria that might tell us they are likely to have a challenge our product solves


Our list decreased from 1000+ accounts to 72.


3. We didn't run ads and send outbound emails, we engaged with the buyers the way they prefer to engage.


We defined one community where the power users and the champions of the existing clients were hanging out and started to engage with the discussions. Then, connected to the most engaged people suggesting contributing to our cluster thought leadership.


That led us to create several viral posts on LinkedIn and connect with strategic buyers.


4. We didn't run a product-pitching event, but invited our solution architect to host an education webinar on solving the most painful challenge.


We promoted the event through:


- Email blasts to existing customers asking to invite their colleagues (for expansion goals)


- 1-1 invites in the community and email (+ LinkedIn for those who were engaged here)


When people were signing up or replying to our outreach, we asked what's the #1 thing they'd like to learn.


5. We didn't pitch anybody after the webinar, instead based on the previous engagement, we created personalized journeys:


- New accounts without prior engagement - checking the product academy where they can learn about the best practices


- Active Focus accounts -> Suggesting 1-1s with our solution architect to audit and improve their workflows."
"Here is what we did with CrossKnowledge team to increase ABM-sourced enterprise pipeline from 35% to 60%:  https://lnkd.in/dBKymbaT


One of the success pillars – weekly ABM pipeline review meetings. 


These weren't just casual check-ins—they were structured working sessions that replaced finger-pointing with collaborative execution.


5 critical components we covered in EVERY meeting:


1.ACCOUNT INSIGHTS & ENGAGEMENT


Sales and marketing shared real engagement data, not assumptions. As Magali (Enterprise Sales) put it:


""We review the lists and say, 'Hey, we see new activity from these accounts—maybe add them to our ABM program. 


And by the way, I've tried six touchpoints with this other account with no response—let's replace it with a more active one.'""


2. ACCOUNT PLANNING: WHAT'S NEXT?


Once we reviewed the data, we planned specific next steps:


- Marketing preparing targeted content hubs with case studies
- Sales following up with Champions to get feedback
- Both teams engaging with buyers' LinkedIn content


This ensured accounts were nurtured strategically, not randomly.


3. LEADING INDICATORS CHECK


We reviewed KPIs to assess progress toward pipeline goals:


- When engagement dropped for an industry report, we immediately improved messaging
- Created briefs with FAQs for sellers to use in communications


This rapid iteration cycle kept momentum building.


4. RETROSPECTIVE: WHAT'S WORKING/NOT WORKING


Quick but crucial discussions on:


✅ What's moving us forward? (double down)
❌ What's holding us back? (fix immediately)


Example: When content production dropped because a marketer was pulled into another project, we immediately adjusted workloads.


5. ABM LISTS UPDATES: ADDING/REMOVING ACCOUNTS


- Added accounts showing new intent or engagement
- Removed disengaged accounts after multiple failed touchpoints
---
This weekly ritual might seem simple, but it fundamentally changed how teams worked together. 


Instead of marketing throwing leads over the wall, both departments collaborated on the same strategic priorities, with shared ownership of pipeline and revenue outcomes.
---
Shoutout to Ken, Magali, Renand and Stapho who made it happen 👏"
"Demand generation from the B2B buyer's perspective:


1. WE WANT A SOLUTION.


The buying group has agreed on the top-priority challenge and the consequences of not solving it now. They start looking for different solutions. 


The vendor that was able to clearly articulate that their solution (not a product) is the best fit for this type of challenge, wins an opportunity to be considered during the next round.


Here is an example.


Our enterprise pipeline declined in 2024 by 27%. Despite multiple attempts and efforts, neither marketing nor sales knows how to fix it. We need a solution.


At this point, Champions might consider multiple solutions:


- Invest in sales training
- Hire SDRs and AEs with a proven track record of selling to enterprise
- Launch an account-based marketing program
- Invest in outreach scripts...


The list is endless.


1. WE WANT A SOLUTION LIKE YOURS.


After evaluating multiple solutions by fit, resources and budget, the buying group makes a decision to select one of them. At this point, they start looking at different vendors and book discovery calls to learn more.


Example.


We want to start an account-based marketing program.


Alternatives:


- Buy ABM platform and launch a program based on the playbooks provided by that vendor
- Hire an ABM agency
- Buy an ABM course or workshop
- Hire an experienced consulting company


Guess what you should do as a vendor?


3. WE WANT YOUR SOLUTION.


After selecting the best-fit solution, the buying committee group present it to stakeholders to get consensus and support for the vendor evaluation. 


This is where you start seeing high-intent signals and generate opportunities.


Example:


We want to hire you as our consultant partner to implement a pilot ABM program. What is the scope, budget, and resources needed?


You need to invest in a fully personalized buyer enablement.


4. WE ARE READY TO BUY FROM YOU.


The buying committee group has approved the budget and the resources, you're moving to the implementation phase.
----


These stages represent a typical buyer journey. Most vendors ignore the first 2 stages and never get into consideration set. They only want to capture the existing demand.


There is another problem: the first two stages could take 9-12 months. But if you ignore them, your pipeline will dry.
---


On Wed we'll go live to share how to build a demand generation model for long sales cycles. Save your spot here: https://lnkd.in/dJYwC3-u"
"Here is a difference between GTM-mature and GTM-immature B2B companies
[analyzed through 10 GTM areas].




*Note: GTM maturity doesn't mean a company's age. 


1. GOALS.


Immature: Leads and MQLs
Mature: Revenue and sales pipeline velocity.


2. FOCUS.


Immature: short-term campaigns.
Mature: long-term programs.


3. MARKETING PLANNING.


Immature: 


-Run a bunch of tactics. 
-Switch focus quickly 
-Try to be on every channel.
-Lack of focus, random acts of marketing


Mature: 


-Excel at 5–7 programs in a few core channels that their buyers use for education and research. 
-Develot joint marketing and sales playbooks instead of tactics.
-Consistent and regular programs.


4. EVALUATING MARKETING.


Immature: last click attribution.


Mature: blended attribution model that includes self-attribution, digital analytics, and customer interviews.


5. GTM STRATEGY.


Immature: 


-Lead generation/sales-led motions. 
-Prioritize broad targeting and volume-based campaigns.


Mature: 


-Understand and focus on their ICP. 
-Develop full-funnel marketing programs aligned with the buyer journey.


6. STACK.


Immature: 


-Purchase expensive tech without robust marketing and sales playbooks. 
-Prioritize automation.


Mature: 


-Develop processes first, then define what can be automated. 
-Start with a lean and inexpensive stack.


7. MARKETING AND SALES ALIGNMENT.


Immature: Siloed teams with different focuses and metrics. Often, one team is not aware of what the other team works on.


Mature: Teams work together on planning marketing and sales programs. Revenue is a core metric. 


8. BUDGETING.


Immature: Only marketing programs with clear ROI get a budget.


Mature: The budget is spread across brand, demand generation and capturing, buyer enablement, and expansion programs.


9. MARKETING TEAM.


Immature: 


-Hiring for roles with broad responsibilities (e.g. demand gen)
-Think the team will figure it out and expect immediate results.


Mature: 


- Start with a lean team. 
- Develop core marketing programs. 
- Develop processes and hire people to own and refine the programs


10. GROWTH PATH.


Immature: Try to figure out everything on their own. Treat feedback as criticism.


Mature: Invite specialists to solve a specific bottleneck, gain the necessary skills faster, and accelerate growth. 


---


There are a lot of other differences, but they usually belong to organizational mindset.


Immature B2B companies believe that there is a way to push buyers through their sales process.


Mature companies understand that the buying process is not linear and is not in their control. 


They understand that revenue comes from brand awareness, demand generation, word-of-mouth, customer advocacy, and a great product.


----

Get a free ticket here: https://lnkd.in/ddZ6Qyk8"
"Here is our detailed Account-Based Content Strategy Playbook
(get it here: https://lnkd.in/dTszwX_8):


1:MANY


The goal is to create awareness with:


- Challenging the status quo of inefficient processes or biases about ""how things should be done""


- Sharing the best-practices to refine the Jobs-To-Be-Done of the target buyer persona


- Sharing the industry news & trends


We target the entire ICP cluster, accepting the fact that most of them are not in the market now and there is no buying intent.


1:FEW.


The goal is to generate demand and get into the consideration set.


We pick up certain operations and processes where a target buyer persona usually experiences the challenges and describe step-by-step solutions for them.


We don't push the product, but on the contrary explain first why and how their processes should be improved. Technology, logically, becomes a central part of it. 


To prove the concept, we use specific use cases or customer stories.


The level of intent is medium, and these accounts could become a future pipeline.


1:1 (ONE:ONE).


We create fully personalized content for a specific account, including:


- Detailed business cases
- Arguments for different stakeholders
- Account-specific recommendations and solutions


We want to accelerate the sales cycle and influence the purchase decisions of the accounts with the high intent.

"You need to report on revenue from ABM, but it is not always possible for the pilot programs. Here are other reports you can share with leadership:


1. TOTAL REVENUE BY PROGRAMS AND TIERS.


Present annual revenue generated from:


- New pipeline
- Deal acceleration
- Expansion
- Renewals


Optionally, break it down by tiers.


2. PIPELINE PROGRESS.


Present the deals in the pipeline generated via ABM including deal status and deal value.


3. PROGRAM PERFORMANCE.


We love to share a simple dashboard with the next metrics:


- # of Cluster ICP accounts (accounts that fit our ICP, but don't know us)
- # of Future Pipeline accounts (accounts that hit our engagement threshold)
- # of Active Focus accounts (engaged accounts with a validated need we work on opportunity creation)


We link them to the leading indicators:


- # of engagements with the target accounts
- # of discovery calls booked
- total pipeline generated, $


4. SALES ENGAGEMENT METRICS.


ABM performance heavily depends on how many meaningful touchpoints your sales team will have with the buying committee groups.


We track:


- Personalized connection requests
- Non-sales touchpoints
- Conversations started
- Sign ups for the event
- Discovery calls booked, etc


5. ACCOUNT ENGAGEMENT.


To keep the momentum, you need to track all meaningful engagement with the target accounts:


- intent data
- replies
- conversations started, etc


and share with the rest of the sales team and leadership.


6. ACCOUNT DEVELOPMENT PROGRESS.


Every ABM program has a series of touchpoints. We present the progress with each of the prioritized accounts.


Depending on your ABM program set up, you can add more specific reports (e.g. 1:few webinar sign-ups and engagement), but the key point remains the same:


Show the impact on revenue and pipeline and show your progress.

"""Let's do thought leadership,"" ""Let's host a webinar,"" without clear processes is a random act of marketing and the exact reason why sales teams push back. Here are 5 other reasons:


1. PROTECTIVE MINDSET.


Sales believe their core asset is their network. Hence, they are unwilling to share contacts or make introductions, assuming their relationships can be ""stolen"".


2. MARKETING HAS NO DOMAIN KNOWLEDGE.


When sales teams talk to marketing and figure out that marketing doesn't:


- Understand buyer personas and their jobs-to-be-done
- Real product value
- Buyer journey and motivation to buy


They treat marketing as an ""arts and crafts department"" and ""cost center"".


3. DIFFERENT KPIs.


If sales have lead gen KPIs, any new marketing program feels like a burden and distraction.


It goes even more extreme in companies where sales don't hit revenue quota while seeing how marketing celebrates hitting MQLs.


4. MARKETING PROGRAMS ARE NOT ALIGNED WITH PIPELINE GENERATION.


Nobody from sales wants to do ""demand gen"", ""ABM"", ""content distribution"", or help with any other marketing program if they don't clearly see how:


- The program will impact the pipeline and revenue.
- Their responsibilities and tasks
- Program timeline


5. MARKETING DOESN'T UNDERSTAND THE SALES PROCESS AND CHALLENGES.


If marketing doesn't initiate regular pipeline review meetings and conversations with sales about the challenges they face in the trenches, sales believe that marketing doesn't care about it. 


Hence, what's the point of collaborating with them?


HERE IS HOW TO HANDLE IT.


1. Make both functions revenue-responsible.


2. Get alignment about goals, challenges, ICP, buyer journey, value proposition, marketing, and sales processes.


3. Fix knowledge gaps.


4. Create a small pilot team (1 marketer and 1 SDR) that will work on a shared playbook on one market and vertical.


5. Adjust KPIs for the pilot team members and refocus them on the pilot program.


6. Document and share results with the entire team.


7. Scale the function.


---
In many B2B companies, marketing teams don't have a strong voice and regularly experience pushback from sales.


Pay attention to the root reasons and handle them as soon as possible.


Not only will you stop the finger-pointing and blaming game, but also create a marketing function that drives revenue.

"The Reality of B2B Marketing in 2025:




1.LONGER AND MORE COMPLEX SALES CYCLES. 


If you're going upmarket or selling to enterprises, here is a sad reality.


Sales cycles: What used to be 6 months in 2023 is now 9 months. 


Buying committee: What used to be 3–5 stakeholders now includes 6–8+ decision-makers across multiple departments. 


Every purchase requires broader consensus, slowing down the entire process.


2.VENDOR RESEARCH HAS TRANSFORMED 


Wynter interviewed B2B executives and published fresh research:


- ""Dark social"" dominates (72%). The buyer journey starts in private communities BEFORE moving to Google or Review websites.


- Reddit is rising as a trusted source. 12% of B2B leaders cite Reddit for unfiltered feedback, with many saying ""Reddit reviews are more honest than G2."" Your buyers trust anonymous strangers more than your case studies.


- AI usage in vendor research has skyrocketed. As Peep Laja reported: ""Our data shows that in 2024, almost 0% of C-Suite used LLMs in vendor research. In 2025, it's around 20%.""


3.MEDIOCRE CONTENT GETS IGNORED. 


If your content is produced by ChatGPT, you have already lost. 


If your messaging doesn't clearly articulate your differentiation and value, you've already lost. 


In 2025, you don't compete with your competitors first. You compete for attention first.


3. RESOURCES ARE TIGHTER THAN EVER. 


With all the hysterical hype about AI, companies slash budgets and resources. 


B2B marketing teams must focus, prioritize and learn how to do more with less while using AI wisely.


4. COMPETITION HAS INTENSIFIED. 


What took years to replicate is now a few clicks away with AI. 


If you don't have strong brand, customer success, and product improvements, you're doomed to experience churn.


HOW YOU SHOULD ADAPT


1. FIX THE MARKETING AND SALES SILOS.


Turn them into a cross-functional team with unified GTM and goals. 


Align on revenue metrics, ICP criteria, buyer journey playbooks, and personalization activities.


2. INVEST IN CUSTOMER RESEARCH. 


This is non-negotiable to understand what topics matter to your buyers, what channels they use, what triggers their buying process, and how their journey unfolds.


3. QUALITY > QUANTITY.


 Invest in ICP-first activities aligned with the level of demand and intent: unique research, expert content, educational events, and content that addresses actual buyer questions.


4. CO-CREATE WITH PEERS AND AMPLIFICATION AUDIENCES.


To get into ""private"" channels, partner with communities, brands targeting the same audience, micro thought-leaders, and customers who can share authentic experiences.


5. BUILD A FULL-FUNNEL MARKETING MODEL ALIGNED WITH THE BUYER JOURNEY.


Create awareness in the right channels, define engagement thresholds, map buying committees, enable your champions with personalized content, and invest in customer experience.

"Buyer journey ≠ your marketing funnel or sales stages. Here is how the B2B buying process happens.


Here is how B2B buyers buy:


-Run asynchronous research online, in communities, or through peers
-Add vendors to the consideration set when they find something interesting or relevant to organizational priorities
-Refine with the team and executives the key challenge, areas for improvement, or key priority
-Research different solutions to their problem and weigh the alternatives
-Loop executive sponsor that owns the budget and agree on selection criteria
-Develop requirements for the vendor to select the best solution
-Reach out to prioritized vendors
-Discuss budgets with those who met initial requirements and left a positive impression
-Create an internal presentation or business case to get purchase approval
-Finalizing the deal with the vendor
-Vendor onboarding


The best ABM teams create buyer enablement programs that facilitate thes stages:


-Establish their presence and engage with target buyers in the channels they use for research.
-Provide an overview of the best solutions and industry best practices through thought leadership and content
-Prepare personalized content hubs with the most common questions, industry case studies, etc. for their Champions
-Update content hub regularly with the newly collected insights
-Create business cases early with the Champions to facilitate internal sales
-Start multi-threading with the buying committee group to create awareness
-Add to business cases implementation plans, cost of inaction, milestones, ROI and other critical documents to address the concerns from key executives
--
A lot of B2B teams still leave in their siloed ""sales stages"" world measuring the conversions between MQLs -> discovery calls -> POC -> Proposals -> Won/Lost.


They don't understand what's happening on the buyer's side and don't influence the internal buying process.


It is a huge gap that costs millions of dollars.

"The truth about B2B demand generation: what we can and can't control + what we can influence as a vendor.


WHAT YOU DON'T CONTROL


-Buying triggers: when a certain situation occurs at target accounts that initiates the buying process


-Organization priorities and alternatives they might consider


-Internal buying process: 
        -who'll make the decision and how fast
     -who'll be involved
     -what questions will be asked about different solutions
     -how vendors will be evaluated
      -who might be against your solution


-Budget and resources


-External factors and market shifts


-Buyer journey: 
     - how they become aware of different products
     - what channels they will use
     - whom they ask for recommendations or advice


-Perception: how they compare you to your competitors.


WHAT YOU CAN INFLUENCE


-Making your target accounts aware of how your product might help with their strategic priorities or challenges


-Being considered as one of the solutions when the buying trigger happens


-Strategic narrative for your Champion to present your solution to internal decision-makers


-Creating a perception of a credible and trustworthy partner


WHAT YOU CAN CONTROL


-Creating content that demonstrates: 
    - different solutions to the typical challenges of target accounts, including pros & cons
    - how-to processes
    - industry best practice, and case studies to get into the consideration set.


- Distributing content regularly and engaging with buyers in their preferred research and educational channels to build awareness and nurture relationships.


-Maximizing engagement and non-sales touchpoints to stay top of mind of target buyers


-Running account research to understand strategic initiatives and key challenges to personalize your solutions for them


- Creating internal business cases and narratives with your Champions that:
  - clearly challenge the existing status quo
  - present the cost of inaction   
  - compare your solution to alternatives with clear ROI
  - pre-address the concerns and questions of different buying committee members.


-Positioning your brand as a solution to the strategic challenges and priorities of your target accounts through thought leadership and messaging.


-Track engagement and intent data for timely personalized touchpoints

"No B2B enterprise buyer wants to receive your outbound cadence.


Here is an enterprise account-based sales playbook we ran with Magali to engage 35 of 130 target enterprise accounts ($100k+ deals).


1. IDENTIFIED TWO CIRCLES IN EACH ACCOUNT.


A wider circle: 8-10 people who can amplify your visibility and trust within the account. 


A core circle: 2-3 key decision makers at HQ and subsidiaries.


2. CREATED VISIBILITY IN THESE MICRO-COMMUNITIES. 


Instead of mass outreach, she focused on:


- Identifying what channels and communities our target buyers use for education
- Map out who they follow and engage with
- Consistently show up where they hang out with value-added engagement


3. BUILT CREDIBILITY WITH THOUGHTFUL ENGAGEMENT.


Magali's activities included:


- Commenting on posts related to their business challenges and priorities
- Sharing relevant insights from similar customer success stories
- Publishing 3-5 content pieces per week focused on their industry pain points
- Running industry podcasts with their peers to tap into existing trust


4. FOCUSED ON BUYER INTERESTS. 


""We value their knowledge and expertise,"" she explained. ""And naturally, they want to know what their peers and competitors are doing."" 


All conversations focus on what they care about:


- Jobs-to-be-done and daily challenges of the target buyer persona
- KPIs they need to hit and associated challenges
- Strategic business goals and priorities


5. FOCUSED ENGAGEMENT.


Magali targeted 7-10 accounts (engaging director+ level, avoiding individual contributor) per 2-month period. If there was no engagement, she kept them on radar but switched focus.


As she said: 


""If there is no immediate buying signal, I don't give up completely. I keep them on my radar. I want them to still see me.""


WHAT'S DIFFERENT FROM CONVENTIONAL ABM PLAYBOOK?


No automated cold outreach and follow ups.


No mass targeting, small batches of 7-10 priority accounts.


No product content, only peer insights and case studies.


No one-off follow ups, consistent 2-month engagement campaigns.


Key mantra:


Building the lasting relationships with the target buyers that continue even if they're not ready to buy.
---


You can't push B2B buyers to make six-figure buying decisions.


But you can stay top of their mind, consistently engaging with what they care about, and earn the right to be considered when they're ready to buy.

"We've analyzed 175 discovery calls from the last 18 months with B2B tech companies ($10M-1B+). Here's what we found (key challenges and priorities):


Developing efficient ABM programs (48.7% of inquiries)


Here are three core challenges:


- Launching new ABM programs without internal expertise
- Scaling existing programs beyond pilot phase to new markets or deploying them with regional teams
- Developing a holistic demand gen & ABM motion


From a Fortune 1000 tech company: ""We have a full brief for a 1:Many always-on ABM program, but we struggle to deploy efficient 1:1 and 1:few scenarios.""


2. Aligning teams around a unified GTM approach (16.2% )


- A significant number of companies are struggling with fundamental go-to-market challenges:
- Developing shared marketing and sales playbooks
- Aligning teams around a unified GTM approach


As one SaaS company put it: ""We need to develop a shared playbook and learn how to collect and share insights between marketing and sales"".


3.Shifting from lead gen to demand gen and ABM (13.0%)


B2B companies realize the obsolete lead gen playbook is broken, but they struggle with change management and making a necessary shift:


- Moving beyond traditional lead generation
- Setting up cross-functional demand gen teams
- Integrating account-based and product-led growth strategies


4. Building pipeline and accelerating sales cycles in sales-led companies (11%)


While it's a smaller cluster, these challenges are the most complex:


- Accelerating long sales cycles for high-value deals ($100K+)
- Improving pipeline velocity and development
- Developing full-funnel programs aligned with the buyer journey


From a senior sales leader:


""Pipeline building is the main challenge. Over the years, we lacked a marketing strategy and the technical marketing skills to attract leads. We lack a full-funnel approach with the correct use of all channels where our buyers are present.""


5. Influencing buyer journey with content (11%).


A small but critical cluster focused on:


- Matching content with buying committee challenges and jobs to be done
- Better enablement for the sales team
- Connecting content to revenue


From a CMO:


""For the first time, we have zero leads in our U.S. pipeline. We've been relying on events, word of mouth, and content marketing. Intent data tools were suggested, but we believe our content strategy needs a fundamental reset.""

"Our last 4 ABM pilot programs generated $>7mln in pipeline (in total). Here is what made them successful.


1.COMMITTED PILOT TEAM.


With every client, we had a pilot ABM team including:


-ABM lead
-Content marketer
-SDR or AE


with operational support from:


-Subject-Matter Expert
-RevOps (In some teams, the RevOps function was executed by the ABM lead).


Pilot team spent at least 60% of its time working on the ABM program.
Commitment is the key.


2.FOCUSING ON ACCOUNTS WITH HIGH PROBABILITY TO BECOME A SALES OPPORTUNITY.


Instead of engaging hundreds of ""it's a perfect ICP match"" accounts, we defined accounts that:


-Have high revenue potential (Tier 1 and Tier 2).
-Know us (hit our engagement threshold).
-We have some level of relationship with the buying committee member.
-There is clear evidence of the challenge or inefficiency that our product can help with.


We ran only 1:1 playbooks with fully personalized content and engagement to drive sales opportunities.


3.MIX OF PLAYBOOKS TO DRIVE BUYING COMMITTEE AWARENESS AND ENGAGEMENT.


The biggest mistake with ABM is treating all accounts the same way and running the same playbooks.


We split other accounts into two groups and ran a mix of playbooks to connect and engage buying committee members, including:


-Cluster (use-case/challenge-based) content
-Cluster webinars or in-person events
-Buyer interviews and collaborations with internal marketing teams to spread awareness
-Constant engagement and content distribution to open conversations


For these two segments, the core KPI was achieving # of accounts that hit our engagement threshold instead of trying to generate a sales opportunity with them.


4.WE TURNED EVERY WEEK INTO A SPRINT.


We met with a pilot team every week to:


-Track our progress and weekly KPIs
-Review and fix bottlenecks
-Cross-share newly collected account insights and engagement
-Plan next week including account engagement, playbooks, content, etc.
-Define and report internally on small wins to generate more interest and support for ABM


---
Most ABM programs that fail usually miss one of these 4 core points. Neither AI nor technology will help you save it.

"Here is how to solve Marketing & Marketing misalignment by setting up cross-functional teams (and then fixing misalignment with Sales):


1. Accept the fact that the horizontal marketing team setup (content, product, demand gen, acquisition, ABM) is broken. 


It creates silos between different marketing units and focuses them on their own metrics instead of pipeline generation and revenue growth.


2. Develop a unified GTM strategy for marketing and sales that replicates the buyer journey.


Every marketing unit should influence the buying process, pipeline generation and expansion, not focusing on vanity metrics (traffic, keywords, etc).


3. Ditch vanity metrics and develop for each marketing unit its own leading and lagging indicators that incentivize the right behavior.


4. Switch from marketing/sales-sourced revenue to ALLBOUND revenue.


B2B buyer journey is a complex ecosystem that includes multiple touchpoints across multiple channels. 


HockeyStack made a research on over 1.5mln contacts from 50 B2B SaaS companies on how long it takes to generate a sales opportunity. Here are the stats:


241 touchpoints and 2672 impressions from the first impression to closed won.


No team can do it alone. Stop the battle and the debate about who should get a credit.


5. Replace first-click /last-click attribution model with a blended attribution:


- Self-attribution
- Digital analytics
- Customer interviews


This is the only way to understand what actually influences the buying process.


6. Develop regular joint planning and review meetings.


The goal is: 


- Review the performance of the current playbooks and programs, and remove bottlenecks


- Cross-sharing collected insights about target accounts


- Prioritize next actions for target accounts: touchpoints, content, ads, etc


- Plan the next week together


- Celebrating small wins and positive signals


---
Marketing and sales silos occur first because of marketing & marketing misalignment.


A lot of teams follow a horizontal marketing setup where different units focus on their own KPIs and metrics:


- Content - traffic
- Demand gen - MQLs
- Field marketing - MQLs
- Client success - NPS
- SDRs - # of lead gen touches & meetings booked
- AEs - pipeline won


They are often not aware of the activities of other departments and don't care about their impact on the pipeline aside from Sales.


Changing people, hiring agencies, buying more expensive stack won't help until you fix the fundamental misalignment.


--
We share the detailed guide on setting-up cross-functional marketing teams here: https://lnkd.in/dxD7khrW"
"Here is an essential change of KPIs I do as an ABM lead for marketing and sales to drive pipeline.


Most companies, when launching ABM, expect new pipeline and sales opportunities, but rarely change KPIs of their team.


Sales stick to outbound daily KPIs: 80 dials & 25 sequences/week.


Marketing: # of MQLs and cost of acquisition.


Here is what happens next.


Sales and marketing continue the old behavior and treat all accounts the same way. The personalization doesn't go beyond programmatic ""FIRST NAME"", ""TITLE"" and AI-discovered challenge. 


This program fails fast.


To run ABM properly I adjust KPIs for ABM team (both for marketing and sales) to incentivize the behavior that is aligned with the current buye journey stage.


CLUSTER ICP ACCOUNTS (not aware of us & product need is unknown).


Goal: Creating awareness.


Leading indicators:


- Personalized connection requests
- Thoughtful comments
- Cluster thought leadership posts produced and published
- Non-sales touchpoints to start a conversation


FUTURE PIPELINE ACCOUNTS (Aware of us & product need is unknown).


Goal: Engaged buying committee + fully researched account.


Leading indicators:


- Fully researched accounts
- Buying committee members enrolled in the playbooks 
- Insights collected from 1-1 conversations


FUTURE PIPELINE ACCOUNTS (Aware of us & product need is unknown).


Goal: Engaged buying committee + fully researched account.


Leading indicators:


- Fully researched accounts
- Buying committee members enrolled in the playbooks 
- Insights collected from 1-1 conversations
- Signal-based personalized engagement


ACTIVE FOCUS ACCOUNTS (Aware of us & product need is known).


Goal: Generating discovery calls.


Leading indicators:


- Fully personalized solution offerings
- Personalized account and buyer-persona content
- Signal-based personalized engagement
- Booked ""bridge activities"": strategy sessions, audits, etc.


---
You can't make ABM successful if your team still reports on the old KPIs. 


Make sure that ABM KPIs are aligned with the buyer journey of your target accounts. Otherwise, the program is doomed.

"Here is what you need to initiate the shift from Lead Gen to Demand Gen / ABM.


1. PREPARE THE DATA FOR THE CHANGE.


You start by interviewing your best customers about their buying process:


- How do they become aware of different vendors and evaluate them?


- What interactions and internal conversations did they have before deciding to buy your product?


Collect all trackable engagement touchpoints you had with them and visualize the buyer journey.


Next steps: 


- Analyze the performance of current playbooks (paid ads, outbound, etc.) and present the contribution to pipeline and revenue, not the vanity metrics.


- Extract the root GTM challenges.


2. INTERNAL BUSINESS CASE.


- Validate the root GTM challenges with the sales team


- Present to stakeholders the root challenges, solution, arguments for it, and the cost of inaction (why doing the change now).


- Present a pilot program, with the budget and resources.


3. LAUNCH A SMALL-SCOPE PILOT PROGRAM.


Define a small but committed pilot team. Set up clear resonsibilities, timeline and expectations. Make sure your executives are aligned.


Your goal: not to drastically increase contribution to the pipeline, but to build a proof of concept.


4. PILOT RETROSPECTIVE.


Document your program and playbooks. 


Present the wins and results.


Explain what could be done better and how to scale the program.


5. BUILDING A HOLISTIC DEMAND GEN & ABM FUNCTION.


After you get initial support, you can start setting up cross-functional collaboration and align your marketing and sales processes with the buyer journey. 
---


Shifting from lead gen to demand gen / ABM is one of the most difficult challenges for the marketing leaders.


You need to challenge the status quo and prove that ""what got you here, won't get you there"".


Executives and sales will be resisting because it's challenging their world of view:


""You say we need to stop our bread-n-butter pipeline generation playbook?""


But if you won't do it, your team is doomed.


P.S. 
You can do it only with the detailed analysis and proof of concept. Check out our guide: https://lnkd.in/d63uPqcC"
"Here is a breakdown of our Account-Based Content strategy
(live overview: https://lnkd.in/dTszwX_8).


Core principle - Cluster (use case/specific challenge) decomposition.


1: MANY.


- Daily LinkedIn thought leadership: ABM, Full-Funnel Marketing, B2B demand generation.
- Weekly email newsletter
- Weekly live podcast

"In Q4, we increased our win rate to 50% from all qualified inquiries because of tweaks in 1:1 account-based content. Here is what we did.


1. BEFORE THE DISCOVERY CALL.


We analyzed all sales calls we had in 2023-2024 and extracted all questions our prospects ask us. 


For every type of question


- how we'll work together
- what can we expect from the pilot ABM program, etc


we created a separate deck with clear answers and examples.


Next, we transcribed all live case studies with our customers and added a short summary for each of the case studies with the link to the full interview and categorized them by vertical and use case.


Depending on the inquiry, we were adding additional content to prepare our prospect for the call.


For example:


- What stack do I need? 
- How to get buy-in from sales?


We sent the content hub before the call and asked to review it before our chat.


2. AFTER DISCOVERY.


For the discovery call, we've updated our questionnaire using best practices from Nate Nasralla and Jen Allen-Knuth. The entire discovery was focused on extracting:


a) The buying trigger and why it's important to launch ABM program now. 


We focused on what's going on, the root challenges and what will happen if the company won't solve it (the cost of inaction).


b) Competing priorities. 


Is there anything else that could distract a pilot ABM team from the execution?
 
c) Competing priorities leader.


Who has a different opinion on how the company's challenge should be solved and why? 


d) Current marketing and sales set up and skillset.


e) What do we need to get the program approval?


After a discovery call we prepared a detailed business case and additional content for our Champion to facilitate internal conversations and explain to the leadership why do they need an external partner.


We updated the entire content hub, including example program timeline, metrics, resources and stack + what we can expect from the pilot.


As one of our clients said:


""All I needed was to make a few screenshots from your deck to present everything to my leadership"".
----
To generate and win enterprise sales opportunities you need to have a healthy mix of 1:many, 1:few and 1:1 content.


Whenever your ABM team starts any engagement with the target account, you must immediately switch to 1:1 fully personalized content.


Understand what questions your Champions might have before even talking to you.


Understand what internal conversations and with whom your target buyers might have.


Create content that addresses the issues that the entire buying committee might have, and update your collateral with every insight collected.


This is ABM 101."
"Here is how I'd optimize the new enterprise pipeline ABM strategy for multi-regional B2B tech company like Agicap.


1. CLUSTERS INSTEAD OF VERTICALS.


Agicap's ""bread and butter"" use case is cash flow management, which could be applicable to companies from many verticals. 


With vertical-based ABM programs you need multiple ABM teams to cover all verticals, while the needs of different accounts in the same vertical might vary.


With a cluster (use case) targeting you can define unified account qualification criteria based on the typical use case challenges and buyer triggers. 


As a result, Agicap can create more relevant messaging and content for a specific set of accounts.


2.SET UP A SMALL-SCOPED PROGRAM EITHER IN GERMANY OR FRANCE.


Starting small in the market where you have a historical success is vital for ABM scaling. 


First, you can collect wins faster. 


Second, you're more likely to demonstrate enterprise pipeline results faster because of brand awareness.


Small-scoped team should include:


- ABM lead - 80% of time.


- SDR with at least 8 months in the position who was fully onboarded and has a domain knowledge - 60% of time.


- Content marketer to execute account-based content strategy - at least 40% of time.


Operational support should also come from:


- Subject-matter expert with deep understanding of cash flow management in multiple verticals. Ideally, a person who spent years in the same position as the target buyer persona. 


For companies like Agicap it's essential because their targeting varies from CFOs and finance managers to CEOs of SMBs. All these roles have different jobs-to-be-done, KPIs and business challenges that can trigger their buying process.


- RevOps who'll integrate Hubspot with other stack that supports ABM program: intent data, field events and webinar sing ups, content downloads, etc. 


This person should also maintain ABM lists and provide fresh updates for ABM team to plan the next account development actions.


- Field events + demand gen team. 


3. DEVELOP AN INTERNAL CENTER OF EXCELLENCE.


The pilot ABM team should become an internal center of excellence to implement a central framework for other regions and teams.


Quite often, the companies that were growing 2x every year, try to maintain the growth with the regional expansion (Agicap started an expansion in Spain and UKI).


The problem with the regional expansion though is that the regional teams often operate in silos and deal with completely different GTM challenges:


Lack of brand awareness, stronger local competition, etc.


If the central ABM framework is not adjusted to the regional reality and nobody supports the regional team, the program is doomed.


ABM requires a thorough cross-functional collaboration that evolves from small-scoped pilot program. The pilot team then takes it to the next level by operationalizing and adjusting the strategy to other regions and clusters."
"Here is how we create an Account-Based Content Strategy:




1:MANY


The goal is to create awareness with:


- Challenging the status quo of inefficient processes or biases about ""how things should be done""


- Sharing the best-practices to refine the Jobs-To-Be-Done of the target buyer persona


- Sharing the industry news & trends


We target the entire ICP cluster, accepting the fact that most of them are not in the market now and there is no buying intent.


1:FEW.


The goal is to generate demand and get into the consideration set.


We pick up certain operations and processes where a target buyer persona usually experiences the challenges and describe step-by-step solutions for them.


We don't push the product, but on the contrary explain first why and how their processes should be improved. Technology, logically, becomes a central part of it. 


To prove the concept, we use specific use cases or customer stories.


The level of intent is medium, and these accounts could become a future pipeline.


1:1 (ONE:ONE).


We create fully personalized content for a specific account, including:


- Detailed business cases
- Arguments for different stakeholders
- Account-specific recommendations and solutions


We want to accelerate the sales cycle and influence the purchase decisions of the accounts with the high intent:

"Creating awareness among target accounts is not only a marketing responsibility. Here is how sales should do it in parallel to marketing:


1. Find the right buyers who belong to the four roles in the buying committee: Champions, Economic buyers, Technical and Power Users.

"Making marketing a strategic function is the most important Go-To-Market decision to grow in 2025
(and how to do it in 5 steps).


1. DEFINE GTM CHALLENGES.


Create a change management group including marketing, sales and key stakeholders.


Analyze pipeline, lost deals, failed programs and define GTM challenges. 


- Sales can't even get a reply because of lack of vendor awareness
- Prospects don’t understand product value, etc.


To initiate the change everybody should agree that the defined challenges should be solved.


2. DEFINE REALISTIC GOALS.


Impatience and wrong expectations kill a lot of marketing initiatives. A lot of companies shut new programs down in a few months because of lack of pipeline.


You can't get a baby in one month by getting 9 women pregnant.


Look at the sales pipeline velocity and revenue metrics. 
Analyze what worked before.
Define low-hanging fruits and realistic targets.


3. DEFINE RIGHT METRICS.


You can't measure brand awareness or demand generation by leads only. Not every program or piece of content should generate a click or convert.


Aside from the revenue report, define leading indicators that demonstrate the program traction and soft brand metrics:


- Message-Buyer Fit. 
- Content impact & relevancy. 
- Brand awareness among target accounts.
- Friction in the buying process.


4. DOUBLE-CHECK YOUR PROGRAMS AREN'T LEAD-GEN.


It's easy to play with marketing slang and call any program ""ABM"", ""Demand Gen"", ""Brand Marketing"". It's hard to maintain them the right way.


Make sure your programs are aligned with the buyer journey including:


- Creating awareness
- Engaging and connecting with the buying committee
- In-depth thought leadership content
- Nurturing in channels buyers use for education and research
- Personalization based on account research


Avoid volume games, and prioritize engagement with accounts that are likely to become sales opportunities. 


5. ALIGN SHORT-TERM TACTICS WITH LONG-TERM PROGRAMS.


Set up realistic goals.


Develop a full-funnel strategy to create awareness, generate and capture demand, and activate target accounts.


Give it enough time and resources.


There are no shortcuts to growing a B2B company."
"How internal decision-making happens at B2B tech companies based on 124 conversations with CMOs in 2024
(and how to influence it)


1. PROBLEM AND ROOT CAUSE.


Senior leaders want to see:


""Our enterprise pipeline declined 42% YoY despite higher marketing spend. Analysis of our top 100 accounts shows only 8% engagement rate across decision-makers. 


Most accounts are not converting into sales opportunities because we treat all of them the same way without looking if they know us and if they are in-market.


We also reach out to one stakeholder ignoring the buying committee group""


Not: ""We need ABM because our enterprise pipeline is down.""


2. PRIORITY AND TIMING.


Senior leaders want to see:


""At current pipeline velocity, we'll miss our enterprise revenue target by $3.2M in Q2. Deals are taking 4 months longer to close due to limited buyer engagement. 


Each quarter of delay means $800K in lost revenue and puts us behind competitors who are already deploying ABM to our target accounts.""


Not: ""We should start ABM because everyone else is doing it.""


3. APPROACH AND EXPECTATIONS.


Senior leaders want to see:
""12-week ABM pilot with top 50 accounts:


Weeks 1-3: Account selection and deep research
Weeks 4-6: Multi-channel campaign development
Weeks 7-9: Orchestrated outreach across sales and marketing
Weeks 10-12: Retrospective, pptimization and scaling plan


Expected outcomes: 


- 3x increase in stakeholder engagement, 
- 40% faster deal velocity, 
- $2.4M additional pipeline by Q4. 


Leading indicators: 


- Account engagement score
- Meeting acceptance rates
- 
Not: ""We'll target accounts with personalized campaigns throught the ABM platform""


4. RESOURCE REQUIREMENTS


Senior leaders want to see:


""We must lock:


- One enterprise SDR at 60% time for account research, development and engagement
- RevOps manager at 50% for tech stack setup
- Content marketer at 75% for account-based content
- ABM manager dedicated for pilot period""


Not: ""We need marketing and sales resources to run ABM.""


5. BUDGET JUSTIFICATION


Senior leaders want to see:


""Investment required for the pilot program: $70K


$10K: ABM stack including webinars, intent data, account enrichment, content hubs
$50K: Consulting company that will train our team and help with the pilot 
$10K: Targeted media and direct mail programs


ROI projection: 


$700k new pipeline within 90 days, expected $250k in closed revenue by Q4 (3.5x return).""


Not: ""We need budget for ABM tools and campaigns.""

"The first thing we do after kicking off a pilot ABM program is creating playbooks...

"Most ABM teams I know failed to scale ABM (account-based marketing) from a pilot in the new markets or with their regional teams. Here is why
(and a step-by-step process we use to replicate successful ABM programs).


1. ANALYZING GTM CHALLENGES OF A NEW MARKET/SEGMENT.


Instead of blindly copypasting what works for HQ, the marketing team should start with the brief GTM analysis of the target market or segment:


☑ What GTM challenges do we face in the new market /segment? Why?
☑ Where should we focus on first? (awareness / expansion / accelerating stalled deals)
☑ What's regional team's skillset and experience of running similar programs?
☑ How are we going to get the buy in from the local team?


2. DEVELOPING REGIONAL / SEGMENT ICP.


Your ICP and its buyer journey can be significantly different in new markets or segments. As a team, analyze:


☑ In what clusters do we see better revenue metrics and have a competitive advantage?
☑ What are the best regional accounts in that cluster?
☑ What channels & communities our buyers belong to?
☑ What are the specifics of the new market/segment?


3. ADJUST YOUR MESSAGING AND CONTENT TO THE NEW ICP.


Readjust your messaging and content to the new ICP by answering the next questions:


☑ What are the “old ways” they are dealing with challenges? 
☑ What should they know about solving their challenges the right way?
☑ What are the regional market and industry trends?
☑ How should we adjust our messaging to differentiate us against our main local competitors?


4. ADJUSTING HQ'S PLAYBOOKS TO THE NEW MARKET/SEGMENT.


Adopt your central playbooks to the current skillset, capacity and GTM needs, by answering the next questions:


☑ What content, activities and channels can we use to create awareness & demand with our regional buyers?
☑ What nurturing activities should we deploy to generate sales opportunities with accounts that are not yet sales-ready?
☑ What criteria should we pay attention to when selecting accounts that are likely to have a need in our product?


5. SETTING UP THE RIGHT EXPECTATIONS AND METRICS.


You can't expect the new program to perform the same way as it performs in your domestic market or segment.


Here are the questions I recommend to think about:


☑ What leading indicators and metrics should we set up?
☑ What should be our realistic expectations?
☑ What are the key reports and reporting cadence?
☑ Who is in charge of keeping the regional sales team accountable?
---
I often see how experienced marketing teams fail deploying their programs in new regions by trying to ""copypaste"" what works on the domestic market.


They often ignore two facts:


- Every market has a different level of brand awareness and competition


- Every regional team has a completely different skill set and different GTM challenges"
"Here is what usually happens to marketing when CMO is substituted or moved under CRO without marketing background:


In this scenario, marketing unit transforms into performance marketing and lead generation unit.


Why?


Because these are the only marketing programs that can be measured in the attribution software and can be ""benchmarked"".


Marketing programs will be limited to:


- gated PDFs to get contacts, mark them as ""MQLs"" in the CRM and route them to sales


- landing pages with a limited product information (no product overview, no pricing) because otherwise the prospects might be scared and won't book a discovery call


- writing scripts and setting up automated cadences for SDRs / launching SDR AI agents


- publish hundreds of articles for the most popular keywords heavily promoting own product


- run webinars that are wrapped as educational events but in a reality are pure product pitches.
----
Most B2B companies that I know that moved marketing under CROs did because if one reason:


Miserable marketing-sourced pipeline.


They want to grow revenue, but don't realize that the marketing problem won’t be fixed by substituting CMO with CRO.


The problem will be solved only when a company has a clear alignment on:


- What’s the role of marketing in the company?
- How to create awareness and demand among ICP accounts?
- How to track, capture and convert the demand?
- Positioning
- ICP and account engagement criteria
- Joint warm-up and activation playbooks to generate new pipeline and cross-sell/upsell to existing customers
- Content quality benchmark


----


Sales can't replace marketing, and marketing can't replace sales. It's a cross-functional GTM team with one goal (REVENUE), but different responsibilities.


Marketing:


- Creating awareness
- Generating & capturing demand
- Nurturing through education content across the buyer journey


Sales:


- Warming-up  & activating target accounts
- Nurturing with non-sales touches
- Relationship and expansion"
"Here are the results of the recent pilot ABM program for SDR who moved to account-based marketing team:


Vertical - Enterprise SaaS (US & Canada)
Buyer persona - Senior HR leaders.


Before pilot:


- Motion: Standard cold outreach (asking right for the demo)
- Results: 0 replies and engagement (90 days before the pilot)


Time allocation: outbound -20% of time, 80% - inbound sales.


After pilot:


Motion: Account-based marketing


Results: 41 engaged & researched account (vendor aware + some level of relationship with a member of the buying committee group).


Time allocation: outbound - 0% of time, ABM - 20%,  80% - inbound sales.


What made the difference?


Our Account-Based Sales Rep (ABSR to make it shorter 😁) worked closely with marketing and SME on account list building, qualification, scoring and prioritisation.


We segmented all accounts (only Tier 1 and Tier 2, I'll explain in the comments why) into three lists:


1/ CLUSTER ICP.


List criteria: 


Accounts fit ICP, but are not vendor aware (no or minimal ""unknown"" engagement) and we don't know their need and if they are in the market.


Goals: create awareness, connect and engage with the buying committee.


KPI: # of accounts that hit vendor awareness/engagement threshold.


2/ FUTURE PIPELINE.


List criteria: 


Accounts that fit ICP and hit engagement threshold we don't know their need and if they are in the market. On a company level, everybody accepts that these accounts are not sales-ready. Hence the main KPI is account engagement and relationship with the buying committee. 


Goals:


- Run in-depth account research to validate the need and buyer journey stage.
- Engage the buying committee with ABM playbooks
- Progressive profiling


Goals and KPIs: # of researched & engaged accounts + account penetration


ABSRs actively work on account awareness and create a future pipeline for themselves.


3/ ACTIVE FOCUS.


List criteria:


Accounts that fit ICP + there is a relationship with the buying committee (good connection) + need is validated.


Goals:


- Account research and buying committee mapping
- Connecting and engaging with everybody
- Posting cluster-based (aligned with the account challenge) nurturing content and distribute it to target accounts
- Create with marketing and SME personalised offers and activation playbooks


KPI: pipeline / new sales opportunities.
—-
B2B companies that will try to ""replicate"" SMBs sales motion for enterprise deals are doomed to fail in 2025 (check yesterday's post from Gal Aga).


Daniel Zsolt Rényi shared that the leading cold outbound agency experience 0.09% email-to-meeting ratio (not pipeline generation).


The moral of the story?


It's time to change your marketing and sales playbooks if you are moving upmarket. Otherwise, you're likely to fire a part of your sales team and miss revenue targets.

Comment here if you'd like to watch it."
"Here is a template we use to do a holistic overview of full-funnel marketing strategy...


It includes:


GOALS & CHALLENGES.


- Business goals: How are they defined? 
- Business challenges
- Marketing goals
- Marketing challenges
- Sales challenges


NEW INITIATIVES


What do you want to achieve with the new initiative?
Where do you need help?
What skills do you need to launch it?


TEAM


What skills do we have in our team? 
Do we have an internal alignment? 
Are the jobs-to-be-done and responsibilities defined properly?
Do we have clear SOPs and workflows for every program we are running?
Do we need to upskill our team?


STACK.


What technology do we have? 
Are we using it to a whole potential? 
Who regularly uses it?


GTM Strategy
- Target markets and segments
- ICP
- Positioning and value proposition
- Buyer journey + channels 
- Marketing plan
- Partnerships
- Role of marketing
- 3 main competitors
- How competitors beat us?
- Where do we overcome competitors?
- Collaboration with sales (1-5). What can be done better?
- Reporting: key reports and metrics
- Budgeting


AWARENESS AND DEMAND GENERATION


- Content creation worfklow with SME
- Content calendar 
- Content distribution plan
- Demand gen ads
- Thought leadership
- Social engagement
- Podcast
- Webinars
- Field events
- Newsletter


DEMAND CAPTURING
- Retargeting
- Content hubs & buyer enablement
- Intent data tracking
- Playbooks with sales algined with the intent level


SALES


- Territory planning and account prioritization
- Product knowledge by sales
- Prospecting routine
- Bottlenecks and dropoffs in the sales process
- Social selling
- Collaboration with marketing (1-5).
- Help they want to get from marketing 


CLIENT SUCCESS
- Onboarding
- Customer interviews
- Expansion insights (how they collect)
- Case studies / testimonials (how they collect and create)


ABM


- Current stage and experience
- List building process (is list shared with marketing)

- Account development playbook


FRICTION POINTS


- Clear pricing or price estimate
- Simplified inquiry form
- Lead routing

"No B2B buyer ever said:


""Hey, I'm interested in being your MQL. 


Please, send me your automated email nurturing cadence and transfer my email and phone number to your Sales Rep. 


I'd love to spend a few hours on a qualification call and then hang out with your Account Executive.""


B2B buyers don't engage with marketing content, sign up for webinars or field events, because they are READY to buy.


They engage because the topic resonated with them, and they'd like to learn more.


We have a fundamental problem here.


Because of siloed sales and marketing, marketers are under the pressure to generate leads.


Nobody even questions the LEAD definition.


Hence, marketing collects any engament (sign-ups, downloads, email link clicks) and handovers it to sales. If, eventually, sales generate an opportunity, this opportunity is presented as marketing-influenced.


But in the most cases it ends up with blaming each other at the next board meeting.


Stop thinking about conversions at each touchpoint. 


Start doing this: 


1. UNDERSTAND YOUR BUYERS.


- What do my best customers have in common? 
- What triggers their research? What attracts their attention? 
- Where do they learn? Hang out? Whom do they follow?
- What are their jobs-to-be-done and their daily challenges?


2. BE PRESENT IN THE CHANNELS WHERE YOUR BUYERS ARE.


Clicks and downloads doesn't matter. Account awareness and nurturing matters.


Stop:


1. Dropping links to your website in every social post.
2. Create mediocre articles based on high-volume keywords
3. Producing low-quality PDFs to collect MQLs and transfer them to sales


3. CONNECT AND ENGAGE WITH YOUR BUYERS.


In complex B2B the relationship is what drives the revenue aside from a strong brand and content.


Enable your marketing and sales to be active on target social platforms and communities to connect and engage with the target buyers, not pitching them.


4. DISTRIBUTE CONTENT.


Creating great content without making sure your target audience consumes it is a waste of time.


Develop a content distribution workflow through:


- Own assets: newsletter, social profiles, etc.
- Sharing with adjustments to the rules in communities
- Paid and 1-1 distribution to target accounts


5. CAPTURE THE DEMAND.


Sales-ready buyers will reach out to you. Here's what to do with the others:


- Remove friction from the buying process
- Do a progressive profiling 
- Add target accounts that hit an engagement threshold to ABM playbooks
- Develop personalized warm-up and activation 
---
Stop living in a funnel utopia.


""LEADS"" are the consequence of brand awareness, demand generation, joint marketing and sales nurturing and activation, customer advocacy, and great product.
---

Sign up and join us here: https://lnkd.in/dp9-3unP"
"B2B Marketing and Sales without customer research and historical growth analysis is a LOTTERY. 


Here are 7 steps to refine your GTM strategy with the customer insights. 


1. 𝐒𝐭𝐚𝐫𝐭 𝐰𝐢𝐭𝐡 𝐡𝐢𝐬𝐭𝐨𝐫𝐢𝐜𝐚𝐥 𝐠𝐫𝐨𝐰𝐭𝐡 𝐚𝐧𝐚𝐥𝐲𝐬𝐢𝐬 𝐚𝐧𝐝 𝐬𝐚𝐥𝐞𝐬 𝐩𝐢𝐩𝐞𝐥𝐢𝐧𝐞 𝐯𝐞𝐥𝐨𝐜𝐢𝐭𝐲.


Look at revenue metrics in different segments and decide what you want to improve.


E.g. We see ACV and # of sales-qualified opportunities in the healthcare segment were constantly decreasing in the last 10 months. 


Why does it happen, and how can we improve it?


2. 𝐃𝐞𝐟𝐢𝐧𝐞 𝐭𝐡𝐞 𝐠𝐨𝐚𝐥 𝐚𝐧𝐝 𝐬𝐜𝐨𝐩𝐞 𝐨𝐟 𝐲𝐨𝐮𝐫 𝐫𝐞𝐬𝐞𝐚𝐫𝐜𝐡.


a) We want to interview top-10 recent customers with a lower ACV to understand why they purchased less compared to similar customers?


b) We want to interview top-30 dream accounts to understand what triggers their buyer journey and does our marketing message resonate with them.


3. 𝐃𝐞𝐟𝐢𝐧𝐞 𝐟𝐨𝐫𝐦𝐚𝐭.


Are you going to run 1-1 calls, surveys or a mix?


Prepare in advance.


4. 𝐃𝐞𝐟𝐢𝐧𝐞 𝐡𝐨𝐰 𝐲𝐨𝐮'𝐥𝐥 ""𝐰𝐚𝐫𝐦 𝐮𝐩"" 𝐫𝐞𝐬𝐩𝐨𝐧𝐝𝐞𝐧𝐭𝐬.


How are you going to engage with target respondents to ensure most of them will accept your invite?


5. 𝐃𝐞𝐟𝐢𝐧𝐞 𝐭𝐡𝐞 𝐭𝐢𝐦𝐞𝐥𝐢𝐧𝐞.


6. 𝐃𝐞𝐟𝐢𝐧𝐞 𝐚 𝐣𝐨𝐢𝐧𝐭 𝐦𝐞𝐞𝐭𝐢𝐧𝐠 𝐭𝐨 𝐩𝐫𝐢𝐨𝐫𝐢𝐭𝐢𝐳𝐞 𝐢𝐧𝐬𝐢𝐠𝐡𝐭𝐬.


During the meeting:


- Rank the collected insights
- Brainstorm what actions you should take
- Prioritize all actions and programs by impact on your goal, intensity, budget, time to value, resources, etc.


Example.


7. 𝐓𝐮𝐫𝐧 𝐢𝐧𝐬𝐢𝐠𝐡𝐭𝐬 𝐢𝐧𝐭𝐨 𝐚𝐜𝐭𝐢𝐨𝐧𝐬.


- Add prioritized programs to your marketing plan
- define a program owner
- create detailed playbooks - don't end with ""let's post on LinkedIn""
- set up a reporting frequency
- set up report frequency and review meetings


The last step is vital.


All ideas without execution make your research a cost and a fancy deck that makes only the marketing team feel proud.

A lot of B2B companies prefer to spend months:


- running endless debates about what marketing programs to run or not to run
- debating what marketing message resonates and what doesn't
- copying competitors or thought leaders assuming that ""if that works for them, it will work for us""


...without ever talking to customers and their ICPs.
