They fraud themselves and rob themselves of revenue.


Customer research is not a ""nice to have element"" for a successful GTM. It is a fundamental operation that should be executed by GTM teams REGULARLY."
"Marketing and sales alignment happens not on the paper, but in the weeds. Here are 2 layers:




1. ALIGNMENT ON STRATEGY.


Before planning any joint program, make sure both teams are aligned on:


- Target market segments or clusters
- Ideal Customer Profile including account qualification and buying committee structure
- Buyer journey scenarios and core activities to influence it
- Segment value proposition and differentiation
- Key metrics and reports, including a holistic revenue report and sales pipeline velocity
- CRM definitions and statuses: pipeline stages, handover criteria, lead criteria, etc.
- Stack ownership and tracking frequency
- Account intelligence: what do you need to know about target account to create a relevant and personalized offer?


2. EXECUTIONAL ALIGNMENT.


To avoid being aligned in theory, but never do anything together in practice, develop joint playbooks.


Make sure marketing and sales sit down together and answer 6 questions:


- How do we select a market segment / cluster where we are likely to get the results?
- How do we select the accounts that are likely to become sales opportunities and define the right buyers?
- How do we prioritize which accounts to focus on opportunity development?
- How do we warm up the buying committee?
- How do we activate target accounts?
- How do we track our progress and maintain the program?
---
Marketing and sales alignment is not a fancy 40-pages deck.


It's a clear agreement and joint programs to drive revenue and achieve the company's strategic goals."
"Before considering ABM for 2025, evaluate if it's a right motion and if your marketing and sales teams are ready to launch it. Here is a checklist we use. 


ABM-FIT CHECKLIST.


1. Long sales cycle (>180 days)


If your sales cycle is short and transactional, I’d recommend focusing on demand capturing activities (ads, SEO, cold outreach) instead of ABM.


2. ACV (average contract value) > $30k.


Will it pay off to proactively market and prospect a specific set of accounts? I suggest considering ABM if the LTV or ACV of your best customers is higher than $30k.


3. Hybrid sales: product + consulting + best practices training.


ABM is extremely important when you don’t only sell product, but also sell your expertise in solving challenges your buyers have. 


It includes product training, consulting alongside implementation, training on best practices.


4. TAM < 1000 companies.


If your market is limited to 500-1000 companies across the globe, you have no other choices than ABM.


5. Multiple buyers are involved in vendor evaluation and buying processes.


If you usually deal with multiple people who influence the buying decision, ABM is a perfect strategy.


If ABM is a right fit, next check your readiness to launch it.


6 QUESTIONS TO CHECK READINESS FOR ABM.


1. Do we have alignment among marketing, sales, and executives on the purpose of ABM, its requirements, and expected outcomes?


Everybody should be aligned on WHY doing it, how to do it, what resources and team's time is required, and what to expect from the ABM program.


2. Do we have clear ICP and account qualification criteria to build a list of companies that are likely to buy our product?


ICP is created for a specific vertical, including:


- Firmographics
- Buying committee
- Account qualification and disqualification criteria
- Account segmentation
- Account enrichment


3. Do we have content for awareness, nurturing and buyer enablement for a specific cluster and buyer personas?


4. Do we have a clear playbook to create awareness inside target accounts, generate demand, and activate them?


ABM ≠ display ads + outreach to target accounts. Your marketing and sales teams must:


- connect and engage with multiple buying committee members
- identify their needs and educate them on different ways to solve their challenges
- create personalized account journeys and offers


5. Do we have a committed pilot ABM team that doesn’t have pipeline pressure and has time to build ABM motion?


6. Do we have an alignment between marketing, sales, and executives on how to measure the campaign’s progress and performance?
----
A lot of teams buy-in the ABM hype but never do a proper onboarding of key stakeholders to get their buy-in and resources. They get a green light to start, but they are constrained on the resources, time and the false revenue expectations.


Make sure your company is ready to launch ABM. Then, only launch it."
"Here is a difference between GTM-mature and GTM-immature B2B companies
[analyzed through 10 GTM areas].




*Note: GTM maturity doesn't mean company's age. 


1. GOALS.


Immature: Leads, MQLs, SQLs.
Mature: Revenue and sales pipeline velocity.


2. FOCUS.


Immature: short-term campaigns.
Mature: long-term programs.


3. MARKETING PLANNING.


Immature: 


-Trying to implement a bunch of tactics. 
-Switching quickly from tactic to tactic. 
-Trying to be on every channel.
-Lack of focus and dedication. Inconsistent and chaotic marketing activities.


Mature: 


-Excel at 5–7 programs in a few core channels their buyers use for education and research. 
-Developing joint playbooks for marketing and sales instead of tactics.
-Consistent and regular programs.


4. EVALUATING MARKETING.


Immature: last click attribution.


Mature: a blended attribution model that includes self-attribution, digital analytics, and customer interviews.


5. GTM STRATEGY.


Immature: 


-Lead generation/sales-led motions. 
-Prioritizing broad targeting and volume-based campaigns.


Mature: 


-Understanding and focusing on their ICP. 
-Developing full-funnel marketing programs aligned with the buyer journey.


6. STACK.


Immature: 


-Purchasing expensive stack without developing marketing and sales playbooks. 
-Prioritizing automation.


Mature: 


-Developing processes first, then defining what areas can be refined and/or automated. 
-Starting with a lean and inexpensive stack.


7. MARKETING AND SALES ALIGNMENT.


Immature: Siloed teams with different focuses and metrics. Often, one team is not aware of what the other works on.


Mature: Teams work together on planning marketing and sales programs with revenue as a core metric. Regular pipeline review and planning meetings.


8. BUDGETING.


Immature: Only marketing programs with clear ROI get a budget.


Mature: The budget is spread through brand, demand gen, demand capturing, sales enablement, and expansion programs.


9. MARKETING TEAM.


Immature: 


-Hiring for a bunch of roles with broad definition (e.g. demand gen) and responsibilities. 
- Thinking the team will figure out what they need to do and expecting immediate results.


Mature: 


- Starting with a lean team. 
- Developing core marketing programs. 
- Developing processes and hiring people to own and refine the program


10. GROWTH PATH.


Immature: Trying to figure out everything on their own. Treating feedback as criticism.


Mature: Inviting specialists to solve a specific bottleneck, gain the necessary skills faster, and accelerate growth. Seeking feedback to improve their processes.


---


There are a lot of other differences, but they usually belong to org mindset.


Immature B2B companies believe that there is a way to push buyers through their sales process.


Mature companies understand that the buying process is not linear and not in their control. 


They understand that revenue comes from brand awareness, demand generation, word-of-mouth, customer advocacy, and a great product."
"In Q1, we pivoted an underperforming ABM program for Testrail to generate 4 enterprise sales opps (1closed won) and 22 Sales-Accepted Leads in under 90 days. Here are 5 things we did that most ABM teams never do:


1. We didn't target verticals, but targeted clusters.


Clusters = companies that fit your ICP and have a similar challenge. We interviewed our solution architect (SME) and defined a cluster where we had a competitive advantage. 


Then, we looked at the verticals where this challenge is more vivid and painful (in our case, regulated industries).


We did together challenge decomposition by reviewing: 


- the broken workflows our target buyers might have
- the root reasons behind them
- jobs-to-be-done and how they might be improved


That helped us to define content topics and messaging that are relevant to these buyers.


2. We didn't target every account that fits ICP, but focused on those who know us and demonstrate product-need evidence.


Instead of targeting a wish list of accounts, we looked at accounts that: 


- hit our engagement threshold
- meet one of the qualification criteria that might tell us they are likely to have a challenge our product solves


Our list decreased from 1000+ accounts to 72.


3. We didn't run ads and send outbound emails, we engaged with the buyers the way they prefer to engage.


We defined one community where the power users and the champions of the existing clients were hanging out and started to engage with the discussions. Then, connected to the most engaged people suggesting contributing to our cluster thought leadership.


That led us to create several viral posts on LinkedIn and connect with strategic buyers.


4. We didn't run a product-pitching event, but invited our solution architect to host an education webinar on solving the most painful challenge.


We promoted the event through:


- Email blasts to existing customers asking to invite their colleagues (for expansion goals)


- 1-1 invites in the community and email (+ LinkedIn for those who were engaged here)


When people were signing up or replying to our outreach, we asked what's the #1 thing they'd like to learn.


5. We didn't pitch anybody after the webinar, instead based on the previous engagement, we created personalized journeys:


- New accounts without prior engagement - checking the product academy where they can learn about the best practices


- Active Focus accounts -> Suggesting 1-1s with our solution architect to audit and improve their workflows.
----
Based on that program, I've created a cluster ABM event template.


If you want to see how it looks like, comment ABM EVENT TEMPLATE and I'll send it to you."
"Most sales reps I spoke to in 2024, told me they hate the lead handoff process from marketing. Here is why.


As one of them described:


""I log in to Salesforce and see a bunch of contacts with a random score. I have no idea what I'm supposed to do with these contacts.""


There are 2 problems:


a) This handoff process stimulates further silos between sales and marketing.


Marketing just transfers MQLs or engaged accounts to sales and celebrates the win. While sales has no idea why these contacts were added, what’s their buyer journey stage and level of intent.


b) There is no playbook to nurture and activate engaged accounts according to their level of intent.


Not every sign up, click or engagement means buying intent. Sales either waste time trying to pitch non-sales-ready prospects or just put them in automated sequence and forget.


The consequences are simple:


- Missed revenue targets while generating tons of MQLs or engaged accounts
- Lack of trust between marketing and sales


This can be solved easily by co-creating playbooks together with sales and align them with the level of intent.


Here are a few examples:


𝐄𝐍𝐆𝐀𝐆𝐄𝐌𝐄𝐍𝐓 𝐈𝐍𝐓𝐄𝐍𝐓 (demand for content).


𝘈𝘤𝘵𝘪𝘰𝘯: A buyer downloads a piece of content, or registers for a webinar
𝘐𝘯𝘵𝘦𝘯𝘵:  Learning more about a specific topic


Next steps aligned with the intent:


- Connect before the webinar to ask what they expect or want to learn
- Follow up after the webinar asking for their feedback, and offering more resources on the topic
- Offer them newsletter sign-up upon content delivery instead of automatically signing them up
- Progressive profiling: collecting more info about needs, goals, and priorities.


𝐁𝐔𝐘𝐈𝐍𝐆 𝐈𝐍𝐓𝐄𝐍𝐓


𝘈𝘤𝘵𝘪𝘰𝘯: Book a demo call
𝘐𝘯𝘵𝘦𝘯𝘵: Get a demo and evaluate the fit


Pre-requisites: 


- Give a detailed product overview
- Explain pricing and ICP. 
- Make sure buyers pre-qualify themselves.


Next steps aligned with the intent:


- Set up automated lead routing and opportunity to book a call right in the calendar of a sales rep
----


We'll share more examples with Vladimir this Friday in our Substack. Sign up here: https://lnkd.in/dSje9cKc


----
There are two rules to fix a broken lead handoff process.


1) Stop tracking downloads and event sign ups as buying intent and transferring them to sales. Instead, match the next step/CTA with the buyer's intent level. 


2) Understand the buyer journey of your ICP accounts (check our guide on B2B buyer journey).


When you map out different scenarios, ask yourself:  


What does the buyer actually want next?"
"Here is a 7-steps Expansion/Cross-Sell playbook I used to grow 4 of my key accounts when I was an ABM lead at KCC and Biosphere.


Note: I've adjusted this playbook to our clients at FullFunnel.io to drive expansion revenue in the tech space.


1. EMBED EXPANSION/UPSELL SIGNALS IN THE CLIENT SUCCESS PROCESS.


I asked CS team to run in-depth customer interviews with Champions and power users during onboarding. During the meetings with Champions, I also touched:


* Srategic initiatives and how they are impacting other regions, business units and teams. 
* Champion's JTBD and KPIs.


2. ACCELERATE TIME TO VALUE.


We incentivize CS team to accelerate time to value for accounts with high expansion potential.


3. TRACKING MILESTONES.


We track customer satisfaction and set up milestone interviews tracking before/after.


Then, debrief our Champion and power users on the positive impact of using our product.


4. CREATE AN INTERNAL CASE STUDY AND UPSELL COLLATERALL.


Even if you under strict NDA, agree with your Champion to create an ""internal"" case study that you'll be sharing only with the teams and units of this account. 


Define which units are likely to benefit from your solutiuon.


6. VALUE-ADDED ENGAGEMENT WITH THE NEW BUSINESS UNITS.


Despite you have a contract with an account, other business units simply might not be aware of your product.


We add engagement and relationship building with the buying committee members of target business units on the channels they are active in.


7. DEVELOP A SERIES OF ACCOUNT-BASED EVENTS CO-HOSTED WITH OUR CHAMPION.


The best way to nurture a bigger group from a target account -> hosting an event (field or virtual) where you address a strategic challenge while your Champion presents how they solved it.


7. STRATEGY SESSIONS.


To create a logical bridge between the challenges and needs of our target buyers and our solution, we suggest 1-1 strategy sessions with your SMEs.


The goal of the session is to audit & refine strategic challenges of other units and show how they can be solved, where our product plays a role as a central solution.


----
Expansion and retention are new revenue, yet here is the reality.


1. AEs desperately send outbound messages to other business units or regional teams.


2. Relationship with enterprise accounts is managed by account owners that don't cross-share the insights about the strategic initiatives of the key client, the value they get from the product, improved jobs-to-be-done.


3. There is no culture to leverage client success process to build relationship with key clients and accelerate their time to value. 
⠀
To upsell successfully, you need:


- Accelerate time to value for strategic accounts
- Build a strong relationship with your Champion
- Start value-added engagement with other business units"
"In 2024, Marketing is often blamed for missed revenue targets. But I never heard anybody blaming the root reasons:


1/ LACK OF CROSS-FUNCTIONAL ALIGNMENT BETWEEN MARKETING, SALES, CS AND PRODUCT.


Marketing, sales, CS, content, product and other units continue working in silos. 


Marketing doesn't have direct access to customers and can only drive inbound pipeline and work on awareness which often is not enough to drive pipeline and revenue due to product complexity and competition.


2/ WRONG MARKETING INCENTIVES.


This year I regularly heard sales complaining about lack of awareness among strategic accounts. But when I dove deeper into marketing KPIs, I often saw the same pattern.


Marketing is challenged to generate ""leads"" or ""MQLs"". All marketing programs that don't have a clear conversion path are either not approved or shut down fast.


3/ LACK OF CLOSE COLLABORATION WITH SMEs.


Most companies we worked with in the past 2 years are selling to technical buyers that are not active on social. Often, both marketing and sales don't have a domain knowledge. Their marketing is based on guesses and general product decks.


This can be solved only when marketing and sales are paired with the internal SME who compensates the lack of domain knowledge, helps with the content and messaging, and strategic buyer engagement.


4/ MARKETING IS NOT CONSIDERED AS A STRATEGIC ROLE AND DOESN'T INFLUENCE THE GTM STRATEGY.


As a result, marketing just receives: 


-Revenue and lead targets
- Broad ICP definition and sales ""wish lists"" from the territory planning
- ""Orders"" from sales and executives for social content, website and product content, decks.


These root reasons create a ripple effect on marketing and sales.


- Lack of joint marketing and sales expansion playbooks to grow revenue from key accounts


- Tech Champions just recommend the product but not helping to sell internally 


- Customer database remains unengaged and doesn't reply to sales outreach


- Missing joint sales & marketing programs with synchronized activities, focusing on the same segments, use-cases and new logo accounts.


- Lack of relationship-building and engaging more key stakeholders per account (increasing buying center coverage)


- Lack of leveraging non-sales touches and doing account nurturing with marketing content


- Lack of the brand recognition and awareness compared to competitors that makes it harder to get meetings & opportunities.


- Extended decision timelines and budget restrictions are slowing down sales cycles.


- Content is product-focused and is not aligned with different levels of demand and intent signals which decreases the efficiency of prospecting and not engaging target buyers.


- Messaging doesn’t fully convey product value to business buyers.
---
The list could be continued, but it doesn't change the core fact.


Fix your root GTM challenges instead of blaming your marketing team."
"We must stop treating marketing as ""lead gen"" or ""arts & crafts"" to drive revenue in 2025.




Old way of B2B marketing:


- Leads, MQLs, SQLs are the only metrics that matter.


- Chasing short-term wins through random acts of marketing (aka ""let's try them all and see what sticks"")


- Relying on last-click attribution to prove marketing impact


- Lead-gen overload: prioritize broad targeting, demand capturing, social lead gen campaigns


- Fancy tech stack first, processes later (if ever).


- Siloed teams: Marketing, Sales, and CS operate like a random guys who see each other a few times a year in the church during Holidays


- Budget: Only programs with short-term outcomes or programs like ""we've done this forever"" (aka sponsoring conferences) are approved. 


- Not involving marketing into GTM strategy planning, treating it as ""sales assitance"" and ""arts&crafts""


- Growth path = trial and error, resisting external help or feedback.


B2B marketing in 2025:


- Revenue and sales pipeline velocity are the north stars for both marketing and sales.


- Building consistent, long-term marketing programs that compound over time and influence the entire buyer journey.


- Measuring marketing and sales impact through a blended attribution model—self-attribution, digital analytics, and customer interviews to see a full picture.


- ICP-led targeting: full-funnel, demand-gen strategies that nurture buyers and are aligned with their current level of demand/


- Unified teams: Sales, Marketing, CS, and Ops align on revenue goals, pipeline and joint playbooks.


- Balanced budget allocation across brand, demand gen, enablement, and customer expansion.


- Rely on marketing intel, customer analysis and historical data to co-create with marketing GTM strategy


- Growth path = invite experts, solve bottlenecks faster, and learn from feedback.
---
B2B buyer process is not linear. You can't expect sales and lead gen marketing to hit revenue targets by focusing on companies that are in-market.


B2B companies create their list of preferred vendors way before they are in-market.


They become your ""Leads"" and ""Customers"" because of successful full-funnel marketing: brand awareness, demand generation, word-of-mouth, customer advocacy, and a great product."
"Here is one tiny naughty truth about B2B demand generation programs that work....




I see B2B demand generation programs working only when they are aligned with the 3 levels of demand.


1. DEMAND FOR CONTENT.


Buying intent: -/low.


Example:


I'm a B2B marketer working for a B2B company with a long sales cycle and high deal size product. I'm interested in upskilling myself, learn the best practices and industry trends.


Demand gen goals:


Motivate target audience to start following you, subscribing to your events, newsletter and engaging with your content. 


Typical cycle: 6-8 months.


2. DEMAND FOR SOLUTION.


This is a stage where inhouse conversations about possible solutions to the existing challenge start happening.


Buying intent: low/medium.


Example:


We're missing revenue targets by 40%. Our outbound pipeline declines while inbound is unpredictable and generates low deal-size opportunities. What should we do?


Demand gen goals:


-Repetitive visits to your website, including high-intent pages from multiple visitors
- Engagement with solution-based content on social and content hubs
- Sharing your content with colleagues


Typical cycle: 3-6 months.


2. DEMAND FOR VENDOR.


This is a stage where the buying decision happens. Buyers do vendor research and talk to vetted vendors. The first vendors they select are the vendors that attracted their attention earlier.


Buying intent: high.


Example:


It's clear that we, marketing & sales, never worked as one team focusing on the same goals and targets. We want to go upmarket and generate enterprise opportunities with account-based programs. 


Which vendor will help us to achieve goals faster with our resources and budget?


Demand gen goals:


- Generate sales opportunities


Typical cycle: 1–3 months.
----
A lot of B2B companies pay attention only to creating demand for a vendor and claim their sales cycle length is 1–3 months.


They ignore the rest of the buyer journey and pay a solid ROI tax on it.


Buyers that are in market spend 6–9 months consuming content related to their jobs-to-be-done and business challenges. Before they become in market, they create a list of preferred vendors. 


If you want to be among them, make sure your demand gen program is aligned with the buyer journey."
"Here are 7 areas of a massive B2B marketing budget waste:




1. WEBSITE TRAFFIC RETARGETING WITHOUT EXCLUSIONS.


Example: I got into a retargeting group of our client because of visiting their website despite the fact I'm absolutely not their ICP.


Tip: Make sure you retarget the right accounts and buying committee roles, not all the traffic that visits your website.


2. POOR CONTENT QUALITY.


Many companies outsource content for their blogs, because ""they just need content."" The content quality is poor, the content is not distributed, and becomes a massive budget waste. 


3. BUYINH ENTERPRISE MARTECH WITHOUT HAVING ROBUST PLAYBOOKS.


If you don't have a robust playbook that you can refine with enterprise software, never buy it. Otherwise, it will literally hang around your neck until your CFO will ask to justify the costs.


I know dozens of companies who laid off CMOs after spending 7-figures on ABM software but never leveraging it properly.


4. FOCUS ON DEMAND CAPTURING WITHOUT DEMAND GEN.


Most of our B2B clients who didn't invested into brand awareness and demand generation, complained about decreased pipeline from demand capturing programs while seeing huge increase in cost of acquisition.


Without investing into demand gen, you literally must pay more to different platforms and channels trying to maintain the growth.


5. SOCIAL LEAD GEN CAMPAIGNS.


One of our clients ran this playbook in 2023. They generated 16k MQLs while only 247 were accepted by sales, and only 4 became sales opportunities...


Huge waste...


6. SPONSORING EVENTS WITHOUT NURTURING PLAYBOOKS.


Most B2B companies just want to get a list of attendees of the event they have sponsored and add that list to the retargeting and outbound cadences.


What they miss is that sponsoring an event doesn't create a buying intent; it creates brand awareness.


The next steps should be account segmentation and qualification, account research, and nurturing engagement.


Without proper nurturing, you just waste money.


7. EXPERIMENTATION WITH NEW CHANNELS WITHOUT DOING CUSTOMER RESEARCH.


We've seen B2B companies investing in TikTok and Reddit just because they have heard on LinkedIn these channels are hot.


The reality was that their audience was not hanging out there.


Don't try to drill a well in a place without water.
---
A lot of teams complain about ""doing more with less"", but often don't see a solution near them.


Take a sober look at what works and what doesn't. Then, reallocate the budget.


Any other areas you'd mention?"
"Here is how to solve Marketing & Marketing misalignment by setting up cross-functional teams:




1. Accept that horizontal GTM misalignment is a fundamentally broken playbook because it's not aligning teams on revenue generation.


2. Develop a shared GTM strategy based on the typical buyer journey.


Every unit should influence the buying process, pipeline generation and expansion, not focusing on the vanity metrics.


3. Ditch vanity metrics and develop for every unit their own leading and lagging indicators that influence revenue.


4. Switch from marketing/sales-sourced revenue to ALLBOUND revenue.


5. Replace first-click /last-click attribution model with a blended attribution:


- Self-attribution
- Digital analytics
- Customer interviews


To make right decisions about what influences the buying process.


6. Develop joint planning and reviewing meetings.


---
Marketing and sales silos occurs first because of marketing & marketing misalignment.


A lot of teams follow horizontal marketing set up where different units focus on their own KPIs and metrics:


- Content - traffic
- Demand gen - MQLs
- Field marketing - MQLs
- Client success - NPS
- SDRs - # of lead gen touches & meetings booked
- AEs - pipeline won


They are often not aware of the activities of other departments and don't care about their impact on the pipeline aside from Sales.


Changing people, hiring agencies, buying more expensive stack won't help until you fix the fundamental misalignment."
"Please, stop calling me MQL and asking your sales team to call me after a webinar. I feel we can easily improve the event follow-up playbook...


The broken event follow-up playbook:


- Mark event sign ups as MQLs in Hubspot/Salesforce
- Starting 5-emails nurturing sequence pushing attendee to book a demo
- Assigning MQLs to sales and asking to call


Webinar sign-ups ≠ buying intent.


Here is how to refine event follow-up playbook to align it with the level of demand of the sign ups and their buyer journey stage.


1/ MARKETING:


- Upload a recording and slides to a relevant content hub
- Download and qualify sign ups by ICP criteria
- Segment all qualified contacts by tiers
- Match tier 1 and tier 2 accounts with the pipeline status and buyer journey stage
- Add all accounts to the demand gen retargeting group aligned with the buyer journey


2/ SALES


- Connect & engage with net new tier 1 and tier 2 accounts who consumed content in the content hub


- When connected, ask for feedback and do progressive profiling to understand better where they are in the buying journey and what their needs


- Suggest ""bridge"" activities (e.g. strategy sessions) to create logical bridge between current buyer needs and your product


3/ MARKETING AND SALES


- Discuss collected insights and move accounts to a relevant ABM playbook matched with the accounts' journey stage.
---
Nobody is signing up for the webinar to listen to the blatant product promotion or high-level stuff that ChatGPT can provide. 


B2B buyers come for practical learnings, connections and entertainment.


Educate -> engage -> create demand -> research and understand the buyer journey stage and current needs of your prospects  -> create ""bridge"" activities / buyer enablement


- 


this is how you influence the buying process with webinars and generate pipeline."
"How will we know our marketing program works if it doesn't generate short-term revenue?


Here are 3 areas to look at and explain to your revenue team:


1. SALES PIPELINE VELOCITY.


Positive changes in the sales pipeline velocity mean positive changes in the revenue metrics: 


- Higher ACV (average contract value) 
- More sales opportunities sourced from marketing
- Higher win rates
- Shortened sales cycle


It's the ultimate metric to look at when launching long-term marketing programs or operating in a market with long sales cycles (6 months +).


You might not drive short-term revenue, but help sales to close more deals while shortening sales cycle.


2. TRACTION SIGNALS AND SMALL WINS.


What was your team able to achieve that wasn't possible before launching a marketing program?


Example.


Before: Sales couldn't connect and engage with decision-makers from target accounts on LinkedIn. Acceptance and reply rates were miserable.


Now: The sales team had 30 conversations on LinkedIn with the target decision-makers. The pilot team was able to connect and engage with 60% of the target accounts.


When you present a new marketing program and explain the big picture, it always makes sense to share and be aligned on the small wins as intermediate metrics.


3. FEEDBACK FROM TARGET ACCOUNTS AND CUSTOMERS.


Embed customer research into the onboarding process and ask customers:


- How did they hear about your company?
- What channels did they use?
- What influenced their decision?


Combine the insights with digital analytics and get a clear picture of what programs influenced the buyer journey.


---
A lot of great marketing initiatives are shut down by stakeholders at the presentation stage just because marketers can't explain:


How do they know the program works if it doesn't generate immediate revenue?


It can be easily improved by:


- Collecting current revenue metrics and sales pipeline velocity indicators
- Incorporating existing challenges into a new program
- Presenting the feedback loops


Prove that you know what you do and keep rocking!"

"Here is how we develop an ABM function.


1. ABM STRATEGY.


ABM strategy includes a fundamental work:


- Internal business case (why doing ABM, how we think about it and what do we expect) to get leadership buy-in
- Goals and priorities (new pipeline / expansion / acceleration / renewal)
- Target market / cluster / vertical
- GTM challenges we are facing in the selected market / cluster / vertical
- Detailed ICP
- Account qualification and prioritization criteria
- Budget
- Pilot ABM team w/roles, responsibilities and % of time involvement
- Key accounts deal analysis to understand buying triggers, channels, key stakeholders and playbooks for ABM team
- Challenge decomposition to come up with program messaging and content
- Key program metrics and reports


2. PILOT PROGRAM.


Pilot program = proof of concept with minimal resources and investment.


You must create a small committed ABM team instead of involving everybody in unproven motion.


Key pilot pillars:


- Small pilot team (ABM lead + SDR/AE + SME) w/ operational support from content, design, demand gen, CS and other business units depending on your playbook


- Only Tier 1 and Tier 2 accounts


- Small scope: 


- 1 program 
- 1 market 
- 1 vertical or cluster 
- 1-2 awareness playbooks 
- 1-2 account prioritization sources (intent/engagement/signal data)
- 1-2 account development playbooks
- Max 10 accounts in Active Focus list (high opportunity likelihood) -> working on opportunity development
- Max 30 accounts in Future Pipeline -> working on account research and personalized nurturing
- Max 100 accounts in Cluster ICP (fit ICP, no awareness, miserable opportunity likelihood)  -> Working on awareness


We never do:


- Invest in expensive technology or programmatic ads - you'd literally motivate your CFO to stay with a gun near your head :)


- Putting sales wish list (no intent, no awareness) into Active Focus.


- Involve entire sales and marketing team - you can't expect them to be committed, it will be hard to get to consensus, and the program will fail fast.


- Trying to replicate targeted outbound + ads to tier 1 and tier 2 accounts - it simply won't work, you'll waste time and the program will be shut down.


3. OPERATIONALIZATION AND SCALING.


When you have a successful proof of concept, you can turn your pilot team into an internal center of excellence.


This team leads ABM motion and works on:


- Developing a cohesive ABM & demand gen model
- Launching new programs
- Refining ABM playbooks with better technology or support from other team members
- Developing new playbooks
- Adapting pilot program playbooks to new markets / verticals / clusters
- Form and train new ABM teams in other business units or regions
---
Jaleh Rezaei described extremely well the current status of ABM: Everyone’s talking about it. Few are actually doing it. And nobody is good at it.


ABM is not a fancy name for your standard lead gen.


Make sure you do it properly from the start, or it will be screwed."

"Here are 5 functions we ask SDRs that work with us on ABM programs to execute to generate new pipeline...


1. ACCOUNT QUALIFICATION.


Before adding an account to a specific playbook, SDRs must:


- Check if account hits all qualification and  disqualification criteria
- Assign a tier based on revenue potential


2. ACCOUNT RESEARCH AND BUYING COMMITTEE MAPPING.


- Define potential account challenges based on the intent, market signals and key initiatives 
- Segment to a right cluster based on the known or assumed account challenge
- Define the right buyers inside the buying committee: Champions, Decision-makers, Influencers, Technical buyers.


3. BUYING COMMITTEE ENGAGEMENT & PROFILING.


ABM success heavily depends on the relationship with the buying committee members SDRs will be able to establish.


Instead of calling or bombarding everybody with cold emails, SDRs should:


- Join conversations with the target buyers on social and in the communities
- Send personalized connection requests
- Do micro content collaborations, involving marketing
- Progressive profiling to understand deeper account challenges and the current buyer journey stage


4. ACCOUNT NURTURING.


To generate an enterprise sales opportunity, a lot of change management should be happened. SDRs should:


- Leverage a relevant cluster content (based on account challenge) to initiate or help with a change management
- Start a thought leadership to raise account awareness and stay in touch by repurposing existing cluster content
- Invite to the relevant events


5. ACTIVATION.


Accounts that are not in market, quite often need a bridge between the ABM program and sales opportunities. SDRs should:


- Collecting feedback about cluster content and events
- Create personalized business cases based on account research and profiling
- Connect target buyers with internal SMEs (subject-matter experts) or peers working for your clients to help with a specific challenge
---
We've worked with 22 B2B mid-market and enterprise companies in the last 2 years who ran obsolete SDRs playbook. Their account-to-pipeline ratio was rarely above 1%.


Whenever we switched to a new model, the account-to-pipeline ratio with Tier 1 nad Tier 2 accounts was always in between 5-15%.


Isn't it a right time to rethink the role of SDRs?"
"In 2024, B2B teams that played marketing Bingo ended up with missed revenue targets. Here is why:


To win in Bingo your skills don't matter. You rely on luck and can increase your chances to win by purchasing more lottery tickets. In reality, it rarely pays off.


This is how most companies did B2B marketing in 2024.


-Targeting a broad ICP and trying to be appealing to everybody with their messaging
-Focusing on 1:many broad advertising targeting sales wish lists and calling it ABM
-Trying to capture more demand by investing in expensive intent\signals platforms and sending 5-emails ""book a demo with us"" ""nurturing"" sequence
-Generating more MQLs through gated to generate pipeline with a miserable conversion into sales opportunities
-Increasing quantity of produced content using AI but at the same time drastically decreasing its quality.


As a result, most marketing and SDRs teams faced a reduction in force simply because it didn't pay off.


B2B companies that maintained growth in 2024 did completely the opposite. Here is what they did (based on our audits and conversations):


-Prioritized markets, verticals and clusters where they saw better revenue metrics and sales pipeline velocity


-Define together GTM challenges and priorities and clear path to solve them


-Created small cross-functional teams that focus on prioritized GTM challenges, goals and REVENUE as a core metric


-Created narrow well-defined ICP with tangible account qualification and disqualification criteria, and buying committee structure


-Selected and segmented all accounts by opportunity likelihood


-Recreated marketing and sales playbooks aligning them with the entire buyer journey, level of demand and intent


-Optimized their stack by using only budget-friendly technology that enables key parts of their playbooks


-Focused on full-funnel marketing operations from awareness to expansion instead of only focusing on demand capturing


-Installed ALLBOUND mindset and multi-threaded engagement where everybody from the team creates awareness, generates demands, engages with the buying committee and collects customer insights
---
""Unit economics"" era has already replaced the ""growth at all cost"". 2025 will be a year of efficiency where you need to generate results with limited resources.


You need to stop playing marketing and sales Bingo and start ""betting"" your time and resources on accounts and programs that are likely to generate revenue results."

"Here is how to build a B2B marketing function that influences the whole buyer journey:




1. GTM STRATEGY.


Develop a clear GTM strategy and align leadership, sales, and marketing, including:


- Goals and objectives based on revenue metrics and sales pipeline velocity
- Focus market segments and clusters
- ICP
- Marketing message
- Narrative (with what strategic challenges you want your product been associated with)


2. CUSTOMER RESEARCH.


Define key accounts in prioritized segments and interview your Champions about their buyer journey.


Here are 5 groups of questions:


a. Buying triggers. 


What leads them to start looking for solutions like yours?


b. Research process. 


How do they evaluate vendors? What information are they looking for?


c. Decision-making process. 


What influences their decision? 
Who is involved in the purchase process?
What questions do they ask?


d. Product value and impact on jobs-to-be-done & KPIs.


Look at before/after and highlight tangible improvements of KPIs your Champions care about.


f. Educational processs.


What platforms & communities do they use to learn?
Who do they follow?


3. BUYER JOURNEY.


You don't sell to companies, you sell to specific people. They have different KPIs, reasons to buy and decision-making process.


Analyze all visible digital touchpoints with key customers. 


Interview Account Owners about deal history.


Combine insights with the customer research and visualize the buyer journey for the most important buying committee roles:


- Champions
- Decision-makers
- Influencers
- Blockers
- Power Users


4. CORE MARKETING PROGRAMS AND MOTIONS.


You don't need 50 different tactics. 


Map out different marketing and sales activities across the buying process that help to:


- Create awareness and attract attention
- Generate demand for your product
- Capture buying triggers and high-intent signals to start engaging with the buying committee
- Enable buyers to sell your product internally
- Accelerate time to value with your product
- Upsell and cross-sell to other units


5. ASSIGN ROLES.


Assign the roles to run these programs and define the necessary skillset. Ensure cross-functional collaboration. 
---


This diagram might be perceived as a linear buyer journey which is obviously not true. I wanted to describe how to align B2B marketing function with different buyer journey stages.


The B2B buyer journey is not linear. Your buyers might skip steps or repeat some steps.


The goal is to ensure that marketing, sales, CS and RevOps work together to influence the entire buying process, create pipeline and drive revenue."

"Expansion and retention are new revenue, yet here is the reality (and the playbook we use.


1/ AEs desperately send outbound messages to other business units, stakeholders or regional teams.


2/ AEs don't collaborate with marketing, but marketing is challenged to drive expansion revenue.


3/ Marketing has limited overview of the deal history and doesn't have access to Champions and power users.


4/ Relationship with enterprise accounts is managed by account owners that don't cross-share the insights about the strategic initiatives of the key client, the value they get from the product.


5/ There is no culture to leverage client success process to build relationship with key clients and accelerate their time to value. 


In these companies retention = locking an account into an annual contract and sending product press-releases.


Expansion = doing same old school lead generation to the same account but different business units.


When I was ABM lead I've developed a framework that we adjusted later at Fullfunnel.io to drive expansion revenue.


1. Embed expansion/upsell signals in the client success process.


You must embed onboarding and in-depth customer interviews with Champions and power users.


Start with strategic initiatives and how they are impacting other regions, business units and teams. 


Understand your Champion's role and KPIs.


Define business triggers that led them looking for your solution.


2. Incentivize your CS team to accelerate time to value for accounts with high expansion potential


3. Track customer satisfaction and set up milestone interviews tracking before/after.


Debrief Champion and power users on the positive impact of your product on their KPIs and JTBD.


4. Create an internal case study.


Even if you under strict NDA, agree with your Champion to create an ""internal"" case study that you'll be sharing only with the teams and units of this account. 


Define which units are likely to benefit from your solutiuon.


6. Embed engagement and relationship building with the buying committee members of your target units on the channels they are active in.


5. Develop a series of account-based events co-hosted with your Champion.


The best way to nurture a bigger group from a target account -> hosting an event where you address a strategic challenge while your Champion presents how they solved it.


7. Suggest 1-1 strategy sessions with your SMEs to audit & refine strategic challenges of other units and create a logical bridge between their priorities and your product.
--
Expansion ≠ 21 outbound touches supported by programmatic display ads.


Expansion & retention = accelerating time to value for your enterprise customers. 


Building strong relationship with your Champion and making him a hero of the organization. 


Developing meaningful engagement touchpoints with other units that are likely to have a similar to your Champion's challenge and create activities that develop a logical bridge between their priorities and your product."
"Expansion and retention are new revenue, yet here is the reality (and the playbook we use.


1/ AEs desperately send outbound messages to other business units, stakeholders or regional teams.


2/ AEs don't collaborate with marketing, but marketing is challenged to drive expansion revenue.


3/ Marketing has limited overview of the deal history and doesn't have access to Champions and power users.


4/ Relationship with enterprise accounts is managed by account owners that don't cross-share the insights about the strategic initiatives of the key client, the value they get from the product.


5/ There is no culture to leverage client success process to build relationship with key clients and accelerate their time to value. 


In these companies retention = locking an account into an annual contract and sending product press-releases.


Expansion = doing same old school lead generation to the same account but different business units.


When I was ABM lead I've developed a framework that we adjusted later at Fullfunnel.io to drive expansion revenue.


1. Embed expansion/upsell signals in the client success process.


You must embed onboarding and in-depth customer interviews with Champions and power users.


Start with strategic initiatives and how they are impacting other regions, business units and teams. 


Understand your Champion's role and KPIs.


Define business triggers that led them looking for your solution.


2. Incentivize your CS team to accelerate time to value for accounts with high expansion potential


3. Track customer satisfaction and set up milestone interviews tracking before/after.


Debrief Champion and power users on the positive impact of your product on their KPIs and JTBD.


4. Create an internal case study.


Even if you under strict NDA, agree with your Champion to create an ""internal"" case study that you'll be sharing only with the teams and units of this account. 


Define which units are likely to benefit from your solutiuon.


6. Embed engagement and relationship building with the buying committee members of your target units on the channels they are active in.


5. Develop a series of account-based events co-hosted with your Champion.


The best way to nurture a bigger group from a target account -> hosting an event where you address a strategic challenge while your Champion presents how they solved it.


7. Suggest 1-1 strategy sessions with your SMEs to audit & refine strategic challenges of other units and create a logical bridge between their priorities and your product.
--
Expansion ≠ 21 outbound touches supported by programmatic display ads.


Expansion & retention = accelerating time to value for your enterprise customers. 


Building strong relationship with your Champion and making him a hero of the organization. 


Developing meaningful engagement touchpoints with other units that are likely to have a similar to your Champion's challenge and create activities that develop a logical bridge between their priorities and your product."
"How to adjust your GTM strategy and marketing programs to new markets and segments to drive revenue (not a frustrated regional team).


Here is a step-by-step process we use at Fullfunnel.io:


1. ANALYZING GTM CHALLENGES OF A NEW MARKET/SEGMENT.


Instead of blindly copypasting what works for HQ, the marketing team should start with the brief GTM analysis of the target market or segment:


☑ What GTM challenges do we face in the new market /segment? Why?
☑ Where should we focus on first? (awareness / expansion / accelerating stalled deals)
☑ What's regional team's skillset and experience of running similar programs?
☑ How are we going to get the buy in from the local team?


2. DEVELOPING REGIONAL / SEGMENT ICP.


Your ICP and its buyer journey can be significantly different in new markets or segments. As a team, analyze:


☑ In what clusters do we see better revenue metrics and have a competitive advantage?
☑ What are the best regional accounts in that cluster?
☑ What channels & communities our buyers belong to?
☑ What are the specifics of the new market/segment?


3. ADJUST YOUR MESSAGING AND CONTENT TO THE NEW ICP.


Readjust your messaging and content to the new ICP by answering the next questions:


☑ What are the “old ways” they are dealing with challenges? 
☑ What should they know about solving their challenges the right way?
☑ What are the regional market and industry trends?
☑ How should we adjust our messaging to differentiate us against our main local competitors?


4. ADJUSTING HQ'S PLAYBOOKS TO THE NEW MARKET/SEGMENT.


Adopt your central playbooks to the current skillset, capacity and GTM needs, by answering the next questions:


☑ What content, activities and channels can we use to create awareness & demand with our regional buyers?
☑ What nurturing activities should we deploy to generate sales opportunities with accounts that are not yet sales-ready?
☑ What criteria should we pay attention to when selecting accounts that are likely to have a need in our product?


5. SETTING UP THE RIGHT EXPECTATIONS AND METRICS.


You can't expect the new program to perform the same way as it performs in your domestic market or segment.


Here are the questions I recommend to think about:


☑ What leading indicators and metrics should we set up?
☑ What should be our realistic expectations?
☑ What are the key reports and reporting cadence?
☑ Who is in charge of keeping the regional sales team accountable?
---
I often see how experienced marketing teams fail deploying their programs in new regions by trying to ""copypaste"" what works on the domestic market.


They often ignore two facts:


- Every market has a different level of brand awareness and competition


- Every regional team has a completely different skill set and different GTM challenges

"Here is a 12-step process we use to develop pilot ABM programs.

"ABM ≠ programmatic ads + automated outbound sequences enriched by AI sales tools to a wish list of 1000th accounts.


ABM is not a substitution for demand generation and awareness.


Here are 5 pillars of ABM.


1. ABM STRATEGY


ABM strategy includes team alignment on:


* Goals
* Segments/verticals
* ICP including qualification and disqualification criteria
* Team
* Budget
* Account segmentation


2. ENGAGED ACCOUNTS SOURCED FROM DEMAND GEN PROGRAM.


These are the accounts that hit a specific engagement threshold:


* Spent 30 minutes on your website reading a case study
* Checked the pricing page
* Signed up for a product webinar


3. ACCOUNT QUALIFICATION AND RESEARCH.


Even if the account matches ICP criteria, are there any other factors that can tell us that this account is a bad fit?


Is there any evidence that accounts might need our product?
 
We collect all the publicly available insights about the target account and map out the buying committee.


This is crucial before defining how to market to every specific company and what warm-up tactic to use.


Otherwise, you'll be wasting time and money marketing to companies that will never buy from you.


4. WARM-UP.


Old and obsolete way to warm up target accounts:


1. Upload accounts to LinkedIn ABM software.
2. Run display ads. 
3. Track engagement.
4. Reach out.


New way:


1. Content collaboration.


* Invite target accounts to your podcast
* Feature them or get a quote for a blog post
* Run market research with them
* Host an educational webinar together.


2. Events.


Create a diversified event strategy, including:
 
* 1:many educational webinars or summits for a specific vertical or roles.




* 1:few webinars to educate target accounts on solving a typical challenge




* Micro-events with thought leaders to meet and connect with target accounts.


3. Social engagement.


* Leave meaningful comments to attract the attention of target buyers
* Connect and move conversations to DMs
* Tag or feature target accounts in your posts


5. ACTIVATION


The last part is matching the insights we collected from account research and warm-up program, and creating completely personalized proposals for every buying committee member of the target accounts.


- - -
ABM is a standard marketing operation, not a one-time campaign , and, definitely, not a silver bullet for growing business.


Don’t buy the idea that it’s a standalone function that can be easily scaled by MarTech software.


The goal of demand generation is to create awareness and demand in a target market.


The goal of ABM is to warm up and activate engaged accounts.


When ABM is done the right way, you can regularly and predictably land enterprise clients and grow revenue."
"When I was an ABM lead, here is an expansion playbook I used to grow revenue with one retail chain by $1mln in 10 months.


For the full context, we were selling multiple household products to retail chains and were dealing with multiple category buyers. They were led by the head of procurement (our decision-maker) and worked closely with marketing.


Here is what I did.


FIGURING OUT THROUGH DECISION-MAKER UNDERPERFORMING CATEGORIES.


For our ""bread 'n' butter products"" we had fierce competition, and it was extremely hard to grow revenue. But there were categories that were overlooked by our categories.


They didn't invest in marketing budgets and didn't focus on engaging category managers.


I selected two categories with a total revenue share in that account <5%.


2. MEETING WITH MARKETING PEERS.


Before engaging with the category managers, I met with the marketing team of key accounts and discussed:


- Upcoming initiatives
- KPIs and priorities
- Would they be interested in growing the revenue for underperforming categories?


After the meetings, I had enough insights on how to present trade marketing programs to my target category managers.


3. ENGAGING AND BUILDING RELATIONSHIP WITH THE CATEGORY MANAGERS.


I started with booking the meetings where we spoke about why the category was underperforming, their relationship with the competitors, ideas they had to grow the category and revenue targets.


With the collected insights, I readjusted my marketing budget and shifted more money to support a few key initiatives of the marketing team of the key account + introducing the trade marketing plan for the new SKUs I wanted to list in retail.


Marketing initiatives (e.g. giveaways at the opening of a new hypermarket) were not lucrative in terms of ROI, but they helped to get buy-in from marketing and helped us to get into their internal trade marketing programs.


The category managers also released the listing fees, which literally re-balanced the negative ROI from supporting marketing initiatives.


4. APPROVING AND EXECUTING ON AN ANNUAL PROMOTION PLAN.


I agreed with our brand manager that we'll schedule and execute an annual plan with the account. Both the category manager and the marketing team of key accounts were happy to see the commitment and additional revenue they can gain.


It also helped us to prevent any competitors' counteractions as they were simply out of the game for that period of time.


---
The moral of the story:


Enterprise expansion doesn't happen through mass emails to the stakeholders of different business units.


It happens through understanding incentives of the different buyer personas, multithreaded engagement, connecting the dots for them and showing ROI with the individual proposals and plans."

What does it mean?


It means that both marketing and sales should actively influence the entire customer journey through full funnel marketing and sales activities:


- Creating awareness and building relationships with target buyers
- Generating demand for your product
- Enabling buyers to sell your product internally with confidence as a solution to their high priority challenges, not as ""nice to have product""
- Accelerating time to value to improve retention and accelerate expansion

"The way how target accounts become aware of product is very different from how B2B teams assume they do.


HERE IS HOW MOST B2B TEAMS CREATE AWARENESS.


Marketing: Write articles and create landing pages optimized for certain keywords.


Marketing: Run PPC ads optimized for certain keywords.


Assumption: 


The buyer is searching for a specific keyword, hence might have a buying intent. They will click the link and will have a desire to learn more about the product.


Sales: send cold emails and cold messages.


Assumption: 


The buyers have a challenge or jobs-to-be-done the product helps with, so they'd be interested in learning more about the product.


HERE IS HOW MOST B2B BUYERS BECOME AWARE OF THE PRODUCTS.


1. SOCIAL / COMMUNITIES.


- See a relevant post (video / podcast episode / newsletter, etc) in the newsfeed (or being tagged) -> check the profile of the author -> check the product


- See an interesting comment to the post of the thought leader -> check the profile of the commenter -> Check the product.


- See a mention of a product (or case study, or use case) from a thought leader, partner or colleagues -> check the product page -> visit the website.


- Asking for recommendation -> Check the product


2. PRIVATE CHATS.


- Peers shared a post, infographic or screenshot from the event -> Check the post -> Check the author -> Check the product.


- Asking a colleague or mentor for recommendation -> Check the product


3. OWN RESEARCH.


From my conversations with B2B buyers, they rarely jump to this step without finishing two prior steps.


WHAT DOES THIS MEAN?


As a GTM team, you need to proactively work on brand awareness in places your buyers hang out and consume non-product information.


To be considered, you need to be known.


Direct ads and outbound support demand capturing, but not brand awareness and demand generation.


To keep growing in 2025, the winning B2B companies adjust marketing and sales to how their customers are buying. They stop running utopian lead generation funnels and their playbooks to the buying intent."
"Last year I've witnessed how CRO shut down the ABM program that drove $2.5mln pipeline in 6 months. Here is why.


The company hired a new CRO who worked for sales-led organizations and had a transactional lead generation mindset. He was frustrated that SDRs didn't generate a lot of sales opportunities despite the pipeline value. 


He thought the core reason was missed outbound KPIs: 


- # of daily cold calls
- Cold emails and LinkedIn messages.


He decided to change the KPIs for SDRs.


6 months later they, indeed, hit lead gen KPIs, but missed revenue targets by 40%.


This scenario happens quite often in B2B companies that don't: 


- define leading indicators 
- align marketing and sales KPIs with leading indicators
- measure marketing & sales success by outbound KPIs.


Here is an example.


Company launches ABM on LinkedIn program involving marketing and sales.


1/ LEADING INDICATORS.


- Personalized connection requests
- Thoughtful comments
- Published posts
- Non-sales touches / 1-1 engagement in DMs
- Researched accounts


2/  LAGGING INDICATORS


- Conversations started with the buying committee members of the target accounts
- Sales opportunities
- Engaged accounts (hit engagement threshold)


The program goals are:


- Raising brand awareness among target buyers from strategic accounts
- Connect, engage and build relationship with them
- Create personalized journeys for the engaged accounts to generate sales opportunities


But this program will never work if it's measured the next way:


Marketing: MQLs 
Sales: Dials/cold emails & messages


Doesn't matter how successful the program is, the ABM team will be frustrated with the results because of missing their KPIs.


The moral of the story:


You always get what you optimize for."
"Adjust your ABM stack to the maturity of your ABM programs. Here are recommendations for 3 stages of ABM:


1. PILOT PROGRAM.


Here is a minimal viable stack that will allow you to run a successful ABM pilot:


- Your CRM
- Miro/Canva to create a visual orchestration of your playbook
- Your marketing automation to extract the 1st party engagement data from target accounts (webinars, newsletters, etc)
- LinkedIn Sales Navigator (max 2 licenses for the pilot) for account list building and engagement
- Project management to orchestrate program and assign tasks
- Hunter.io / Clay to find emails


Optional:


- Aligned for sales enablement
- Intent data(Dealfront)


Most of this software you already have. The rest will cost you max $200/month.


Next steps:


- Launch a small-scoped pilot with a minimal stack
- Document all of your processes and outcomes
- Define the processes or workflows that could be refined and/or accelerated
- Search for software that can help with it.


That way you develop a successful program by gradually building your processes and stack instead of ramping up budget and setting up unrealistic expectations.


KEEP IN MIND!


You can (and should) launch your first ABM campaign without a stack.


The lowest hanging fruit is deal expansion, deal acceleration, or re-engagement campaign.


2. OPERATIONALIZING ABM.


At this stage you invest into documenting your playbooks and onboarding rest of the team. You can also refine some of your ABM operations.


You can add: 


- more sources of intent and engagement data (G2, Mention, BuiltWith)
- more advanced enrichment software (Cognism or ZoomInfo)
- set up ABM operations and reporting in HubSpot


Core goal: make your playbooks streamlined, less time-consuming and with all data coming to your CRM.


3. SCALING ABM.


When ABM becomes your core motion with cross-functional collaboration across teams, you can invest into more expensive stack.


Goals: enable global teams to use one single of truth to run ABM programs.


Consider investing into:


- ABM orchestration, tracking and account engagement software (Demandbase) 
- Programmatic multichannel ads (Demandbase)
- Personalized gifting (Reachdesk)
- Sales playbooks (Outreach)


---
 
Don't build a stack and don't invest in expensive software before creating ABM processes and onboarding marketing, and sales teams.
 
The software can refine and accelerate ABM processes, but you need to develop the processes first!


Strategy -> Resources -> Pilot -> Process -> Stack.

"We should move away from siloed goal/KPIs setting for marketing and sales and focus on revenue metrics and pipeline velocity to define our targets...


TRADITIONAL GOAL SETTING


Marketing


- Generate MQLs under target CAC
- Distribute budget across demand capturing/lead gen activities: ads, SEO, tradeshows and conferences


Sales


- Hit revenue targets
- Hit outbound KPIs: dials, cold emails and messages


This framework puts both teams in the lead generation hamster wheel and prioritizes the siloed work.


Outcomes:


- Missed annual company revenue target
- Celebrating individual contributors aka top performers while creating frustration across teams
- Blaming and fingerpointing between marketing and sales during the annual review meetings


I firmly believe that every B2B company that sells to mid-market/enterprise orgs should flip the funnel and start from revenue metrics and pipeline velocity analysis.


Then, do the revenue decomposition by markets, segments and account tiers.


ACCOUNT-BASED GOAL SETTING


Here are the questions that both marketing and sales should answer together:


1/ How our revenue metrics look like across different markets, verticals, tiers and clusters? 


- ACV
- Sales cycle length
- Total revenue
- Win rate
- # of new qualified sales opportunities
- Successful use cases
- Churn


2/ How should we distribute revenue targets among: 


- new customers (new revenue)
- current pipeline (acceleration)
- existing customers (expansion) considering historical churn?


3/ How can we distribute new pipeline revenue targets between Tier 1, Tier 2 and Tier 3 accounts?


4/ How many sales opportunities do we need to generate across different these three tiers?


5/ What is (or might be) our account-to-opportunity conversion? How many accounts should we actively target?


6/ How can we identify accounts with a high likelihood to become sales opportunities? What criteria should they match?


7/ What programs should we run to drive awareness and generate demand from these accounts?


Getting clear answers helps both marketing and sales to get on the same page and develop a clear path to revenue targets. 


It also shifts their approach from ""doing everything at scale"" and prioritizing volume to:


What are the best activities across the full funnel that are aligned with the buyer journey of our target accounts.
----
Getting more budget for air cover and doing more outbound touches is not a panacea to revenue gaps.


This is rather the fastest way to burn out and demotivate the entire GTM team.


Putting revenue metrics in front of them and doing full funnel revenue targets decomposition together is what helps teams to actually achieve the results."
"Back to my corporate days, I used this simple spreadsheet to budget and forecast my ABM program. Here is a step-by-step breakdown.


(The template with more details on planning and budgeting: https://lnkd.in/dn6pEQCi)


1. TIER SEGMENTATION.


- Export all accounts and segment them by total revenue
- Add one more column with accumulative revenue
- Define tiers of accounts


To define the tier, I look at the drop in revenue share. 


E.g. Customer #3 generates 15% of revenue. Customer #4 has a 7% share, which means a significant drop. 


I define Tier 3 when reaching 80% of accumulative revenue.


2. CALCULATE TIER ACV (AVERAGE CONTRACT VALUE).


The formula is simple: total revenue / # of accounts.


3. DEFINE TIER BUDGET.


Would you be willing to spend more on generating $500k deals instead of $50k?


The answer is obvious, but most companies never do it. They allocate budget based on average CAC (cost of acquisition). 


I usually check unit economics with CFO to define how much we can afford to spend on one account to generate a sales opportunity (cost of opportunity).


Example Cost Per Opportunity:


Tier 1: $3.500 
Tier 2: $1000
Tier 3: $300


4. MATCH # OF ACCOUNTS ACROSS TIERS WITH REVENUE TARGETS AND TEAM CAPACITY.


Avoid temptation to add hundreds of tier 3 accounts.


a) It won't pay off, and you'll never be able to engage them meaningfully. Add them to the demand gen layer.


b) Add margin of safety (e.g. 30%) to ensure that you have enough accounts with a decent revenue potential to hit revenue targets.


5. MAKE A FORECAST BASED ON REVENUE METRICS.


Look across tiers at:


- Win rates
- Sales cycle length
- ACV
- Account-to-pipeline ratio (if you already run ABM)


6. CALCULATE THE TOTAL BUDGET.


I just sum the budget between tiers.


7. ALIGN BUDGET WITH ABM PROGRAM AND PLAYBOOKS.


Make sure you avoid overinvesting into technology and programmatic display ads. Ensure, your budget allow you to run meaningful touchpoints with the target accounts.


---


This budgeting framework requires a thorough analysis of sales pipeline velocity and revenue metrics. 


It takes time but it helps to plan realistic programs. 


It also focuses your team on selecting accounts with a high probability to become a sales opportunity instead of marketing to a ""wish list""."
"The failed ABM programs we audited in 2024 have one thing in common - missing one of these pillars:


1. PROGRAM GOALS ALIGNED WITH STRATEGIC INITIATIVES.


There are 4 goals for ABM programs:


- Net-new pipeline
- Pipeline acceleration - closing existing deals
- Expansion
- Renewal


Often, ABM teams focus on net-new pipeline instead of talking to key stakeholders and sales, and define what has a higher priority for them. Don't do anything that is misaligned with strategic initiatives.


Also, ensure that everybody understands the WHY behind your program and have the right expectations.


2. PROGRAM ICP.


Instead of ""we want to target the biggest accounts in our area"", you need to define clear criteria for account selection.


Litmus test question:


If I was going to bet my compensation on particular accounts, which criteria would they match?


Include:


- Firmographics
- Buying committee
- Account qualification
- Account segmentation
- Buying journey


3. ACCOUNT LIST BUILDING.


Not all accounts are sales-ready. Think about account selection criteria the next way:


- Revenue potential
- Relationship
- Vendor awareness
- Product need evidence / Buying signals


Then, think about what sources you can use to define these accounts.


4. ACCOUNT RESEARCH.


This is the most ignored step. It's time-consuming but without account research you can't personalize your account journey.


Think about:


- What is absolutely MUST KNOW information about target accounts we need to collect to personalize our proposal?
- How can we get it?


5. ACCOUNT DEVELOPMENT (WARM-UP & ACTIVATION)


ABM ≠ programmatic display ads, landing pages and automated outreach sequence. 


Make sure your account development playbook includes:


- Warm-up: how marketing and sales will create awareness with buyers, connect and engage with them
- Activation: how sales should activate accounts
- Nurturing: how marketing and sales will stay in touch with target accounts


6. TEAM.


Make sure you have at least 3 committed people running the ABM program for at least 50% of their time:


- ABM lead
- Sales rep (SDR or AE)
- Subject-matter expert


With partial operational support from:


- RevOps
- Content & design
- Demand gen


7. STACK


Everybody wants to jump here, but technology only enables the processes above, not replaces them.


Define only the tools that without overpaying help to:


- Track 1st party account engagement (intent data)
- Enrich accounts and define right buying committee members
+ the rest to support your playbook.


Start small, and build graudally.


8. REPORTS & METRICS.


Define key metrics and leading indicators for your program goals. Make sure everybody accepts them, because revenue and pipeline won't be generated immediately.


Create simple dashboards to track program performance.
---
We'll cover a step-by-step process for planning a pilot ABM program for 2025 in two weeks. Save your spot here: https://lnkd.in/dDQhWZkm"
"We made a simple change to drive more pipeline and revenue from ABM programs:




Turning every week into a small sprint.


In a recent project, we set a weekly cadence of 60-mins Monday meetings.


Agenda:


SDR shares the insights from the conversations with the target accounts and account research. Next, share what he/she might need for particular accounts to proceed with nurturing or activation.


AE shares the insights from pipeline deals or conversations with new buying committee groups of the existing accounts. Same, next, he/she shares the needs and ideas to influence the deals.


RevOps share the account engagement insights from the past week (high-intent pages visits, event sign-ups, new high-engaged accounts, etc.).


ABM lead structures and prioritizes with the team all collected insights and creates a sprint for the next week.


Sprint includes:


- Exact content the content team should create to drive new pipeline, nurture accounts or accelerate existing deals
- Ads to target particular accounts
- Accounts & buyers SDR should engage with the particular actions, not ""I wanted to check in""
- Actions for AE


This simple tweak helped us to do the right action at the right time instead of following the ""waterfall"" plan where all teams work in silos. 


Ultimately, it's about ensuring marketing and sales work together on the same goals in the trenches, instead of being aligned on PowerPoint deck"
"The SDR playbook B2B companies were running for decades led to laying off 236k SDRs last year. Here is how we regroup SDR function:

They evaluate ICP fit and revenue potential, and subsegment all qualified accounts into two lists.


Active Focus and Future pipeline.


3. 𝐕𝐨𝐥𝐮𝐦𝐞-𝐛𝐚𝐬𝐞𝐝 𝐊𝐏𝐈𝐬 -> 𝐐𝐮𝐚𝐥𝐢𝐭𝐲-𝐛𝐚𝐬𝐞𝐝 𝐊𝐏𝐈𝐬 𝐟𝐨𝐫 𝐝𝐢𝐟𝐟𝐞𝐫𝐞𝐧𝐭 𝐚𝐜𝐜𝐨𝐮𝐧𝐭 𝐥𝐢𝐬𝐭𝐬.


For the «Active Focus List», ABSR do:


- Account research and buying committee mapping
- Connecting and engaging with everybody
- Posting cluster-based (aligned with the account challenge) nurturing content and distribute it to target accounts
- Create with marketing and SME personalised offers and activation playbooks


KPI: pipeline.


We have implemented this model with several clients lsat year, and saw account-to-pipeline 5-15%.


For the «Future pipeline», ABSRs:


- Run account research and define blind spots:
- Connect and engage with the buying committee 
- Progressive profiling


KPI: account engagement and relationship with the buying committee. 


ABSRs actively work on account awareness and create a future pipeline for themselves.


—-
The detailed guide on Account-Based Sales Rep function is here: https://lnkd.in/eXin7VNF"
"Here are the keys to running a successful ABM program shared by marketing leaders during our ABM workshop in Amsterdam.


Eva De Blander: switch to challenge-based targeting and nurturing. 99% of your success lies in nailing down ABM fundamentals and preparation.


Kristina Selviesiuk: Account lists are not static, they move and evaluate. A company which was disqualified can move fast to account focus segment. Never do ABM for Tier 3, only Tier 1 and 2.


Eppo H.: Focus your efforts on asymmetries between access to your solution and the problems of your audiences.


Sarah Stockhem: Activate accounts before webinars to get insights on their pain points and use it as an opportunity to engage them after


Joyce Groenewegen: ABM is teamwork and important to take at the account together with sales. Start small with proof of concept and expand when its succesfull.


Andrei Iocin: ABM needs expectations management before it even starts. Account lists needs weekly updates. Collaboration between marketing, sales, revops, content and product is key.


Sébastien Galand: Going through the whole process matters, don’t jump to solutions. Process must be iterative.


Dorus Kaandorp: Focus not only on LinkedIn and email when targeting accounts. Check for ‘shortcuts’ within current relationships.


Pim Hogeweg: Random input = random output. Get your ABM fundamentals sorted, create alignment around that in your team and enjoy a focused journey towards selling to your most promising accounts.


Dimitar Serafimov: Process, discipline and patience is key. Wide company buy-in is also crucial.


Agnieszka Sobala: Not skipping the „obvious“ steps as selecting the buyer and ICP


Dónal Ó Mearáin: Focus 80% effort on active prospects.


Rihab H.: Know your ICP, do the challenge composition exercise and build content and engagement based on these challenges (and monitor the results).


Dunja Radulov: Focus on the strategic challenge of target accounts when building clusters.


Shantanu Verma:  Setting expectations before launching the ABM campaign on time to ROI. 


Carlos Veerman: Think from different perspectives, not just from your own role within an organization when planning ABM program. 


Xander Wegscheider: Sitting together exchanging lists does not equal proper collaboration(siloes still exist).


Mihnea Popa: Personalization can be very small but gotta be very meaningful. 


Paul Hassels Mönning:


The real ABM work starts in maintenance. ABM is teamwork. ABM is a dynamic game, refresh & update weekly.


Stefana Sopco: Aligning teams is way more difficult than it looks like. Everyone wants smth different even though we have the same target.


Creating alignment between the teams requires constant communications and transparent knowledge sharing.
---
My 5 cents - ABM is a strategic motion, not a technology + programmatic display ads"" + automated ""personalized"" outbound.


Make it a part of cross-functional collaboration, not a siloed campaign that will fail.
